Et modus operandi in incisione eius est: ut ponat infirmus caput suum in sinu tuo.	And the method of operation in its cutting is: that the sick person should place his head in your lap. 
Deinde aperi oculos eius, et eleua palpebram manu tua.	Then open his eyes, and lift his eyelid with your hand.  
Deinde collige ungulam cum uncino paucae duplationis, et extende eam ad superiora.	Then collect the nail with a hook of few twirls, and extend it upwards. 
Deinde accipe acum, et intromitte in eam pilum ex pilis equi, et bouis, aut uaccae: et sit filum forte, et duplica extremitatem acus parumper, et fige eam in medio ungulae: et penetra eam cum acu, et liga cum filo ungulam, et extende eam ad superiora: et excoria cum pilo latus ungulae quod sequitur pupillam, ac si tu serres eam cum pilo usque ad postreimnum eius.	Then take a needle, and insert into it a hair from the hairs of a horse, ox, or cow; and let the thread be strong, and double the extremity of the needle a little, and fix it in the middle of the nail; and pierce it with the needle, and bind the nail with thread, and extend it upwards; and flay the side of the nail which follows the pupil with the hair as if you were to press it with the hair up to its last part.  
Deinde incide residuum in radice lachrymalis cum spatumili subtili, aut cum forficibus paruis: et dimitte carnem lachrymalis naturalem, ut non accidat ex incisione eius cursus lachrymarum assiduus.	Then cut the remainder at the root of the lacrimal with a fine scalpel, or with small forceps; and let the natural lacrimal flesh be released so that a constant flow of tears does not occur from its incision.  
Et quandoque extenditur ungula cum uncino solo: aut cum filo, sicut diximus.	And sometimes the nail is extended with a hook alone; or with thread as we have said. 
Deinde excoriatur cum spatumili leni, cuius haec est forma.	Then flay it with a gentle scalpel, which has this form.  
Et caue, ne tangat spatumile tunicam corneam, et accidat in ea ruptura, et perforetur pupilla.	And beware that the scalpel does not touch the corneal tunic, and a rupture occurs in it, and the pupil is perforated.  
Deinde post incisionem, proice in oculum aliquid salis contriti, aut ex sief facto ex ziniar, et dimitte ipsum usque ad diem alium.	Then after the incision, throw into the eye something ground salt, or made from alum, and let it remain until the next day. 
Deinde cura ipsum cum eo quod oportet, usquequo sanetur.	Then care for it with what is necessary until it heals. 
Quod si ungula est non neruosa, et non potes intromittere in eam acum, neque figitur in ea uncinus, tunc multotiens curatur haec species ungulae cum medicinis, et sanatur sicut narraui in diuisione.	But if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert a point into it nor does a hook catch in it, then this type of nail is often cured with medicines and heals as I have described in the division.  
Quod si uis incidere eam, tunc aperi oculum infirmi, et accipe spatumile subtile, lene, debilis acuitatis, secundum hanc formam.	But if you wish to cut it, then open the eye of the infirm person and take a delicate spatula, soft, weak in sharpness, according to this form. 
Et rade ungulam desuper rasione cum subtilitate.	And scrape the nail from above with subtlety.  
Quod si uides quod ipsa rarificatur et confringitur, et imprimit in eam rasio, tunc distilla ex hora tua in oculum ex sief facto ex ziniar, aut ex sief rubeo, aut sale trito: et opila oculum usque ad diem alium.	But if you see that it thins and breaks, and the scraper presses into it, then distill from your hour into the eye alum made water, or red alum water, or ground salt: and bind the eye until the next day.  
Deinde itera super ipsam operationem, donec remoueatur totum eius.	Then repeat the operation over it until all of it is removed. 
Nisi contrarium sit tibi in oculo apostema calidum: tunc enim dimitte ipsam, et cura apostema, donec sanetur.	Unless there is a hot abscess in your eye: then let it alone and care for the abscess until it heals. 
Deinde itera operationem super ipsam cum rasione, donec sanetur.	Then repeat the operation over it with a scraper until it heals. 
Eminentia autem carnis lachrymalis, si nocet in oculo nocumento magno, suspendatur cum uncino, et incide ex ea partem eius: et non ultimes incisionem, ut non accidat cursus lachrymarum.	But if the prominence of the tear duct causes great harm to the eye, suspend it with a hook and cut out a portion of it; and do not finish the incision so that the course of tears does not happen. 
Deinde stilla in lachrymale sief rubeum, aut factum ex ziniari, donec sanetur.	Then still red alum water or water made from alum into the tear duct until it heals.  
¶ De incisione Alguardenic, et carne nata in oculo.	Of the incision of a foreign body and flesh born in the eye. 
Caput XVII.	Chapter Seventeen. 
Nascitur quandoque in quibusdam oculis hominum caro rubea composita, uel superposita, donec cooperit pupillam, aut appropinquat, aut stringit super palpebras, et fortasse conuertit palpebras ad exteriora: et assimilatur rosae balaustinae.	Sometimes red flesh grows in the eyes of men, composed or superimposed, until it covers the pupil or approaches and presses upon the eyelids and perhaps turns the eyelids outward; and it is likened to a rose baluster. 
Et operatio in ea etiam est, ut ponat infirmus caput suum in sinu tuo.	And the operation on it is also that the sick person puts his head on your lap. 
Deinde aperi oculos eius, et collige illam carnem totam cum uncinis conuenientibus ad illud: et tene illud cum forcipe uno, aut gesti.	Then open his eyes, and gather all that flesh with suitable hooks: and hold it with one forceps, or hand. 
Deinde incide carnem in primis, donec finiatur totum eius cum incisorio.	Then cut the flesh first, until all of it is finished with a scalpel. 
Et caue ab oculo, ut non laedas ipsum apud operationem: et sit incisio tua qua ipsam incidis, aut cum spatumili, quod narrauimus in incisione ungulae: aut cum forficibus paruis, cum quibus colligitur asebel, secundum quod ueniet forma eius post hoc capitulum.	And be careful from the eye, so that you do not injure it during the operation: and let your incision be as you cut it, either with a scalpel, which we have described in the incision of the nail; or with small forceps, with which the asebel is collected, according to its shape after this chapter.  
Cum ergo completur incisio tua, et remouetur tota alguardenici, tunc imple oculum ex sale contrito: aut distilla in eum puluerem rubeum, et similia illi ex medicinis corrosiuis: et pone super oculum deforis cottum cum albugine oui: ut securetur ab apostemate calido.	When therefore your incision is complete, and all the chalazion is removed, then fill the eye with crushed salt; or distill into it red powder, and the like corrosive medicines from it: and place cotton wool with egg white on the eye outside; so that it is protected from a hot abscess.  
Quod si remanet ex alguardenici aliquid, et dominatur tibi sanguis calidus, et times apostema calidum: tunc dimitte oculum, et cura ipsum cum eo quod sedat apostema.	But if anything remains from the chalazion, and hot blood dominates you, and you fear a hot abscess: then let go of the eye, and treat it with that which calms the abscess. 
Deinde itera super ipsum cum operatione, donec sanetur.	Then repeat the operation on it until it is healed.  
Et similiter fac cum carne addita quae accidit in oculo ex hac specie.	And do likewise with the added flesh that occurs in the eye from this kind. 
Verumtamen oportet, ut alienes curationem omnis oculi debilis ex uia naturali, aut ex uia accidentali, operando cum ferro: et non intromittas manum tuam in aliqua harum operationum, donec uideas, quod illud membrum est tolerans illam operationem.	However, it is necessary that others treat the cure of all weak eyes from natural or accidental ways by operating with iron: and do not put your hand into any of these operations until you see that the member can tolerate the operation.
¶ De collectione Sebel ex oculo.	On the Gathering of an Asebel from the Eye. 
Caput XVIII.	Chapter XVIII. 
Sebel sunt uenae rubeae quae texuntur super oculum, et prohibent uisui operationem suam: et debilitant oculum cum longitudine dierum.	Asebels are red veins that are woven over the eye, and prevent vision from its operation: and they weaken the eye with the length of days.  
Necesse est ergo tibi in primis, ut consideres, si oculus in quo est Sebel, est fortis, et non est in eo aegritudo aliqua, praeter Sebel: tunc collige Sebel eius.	Therefore it is necessary for you first to consider whether the eye in which there is an asebel is strong and there is no sickness in it except for the asebel: then gather its asebel.
Et est, ut praecipias infirmo, ut ponat caput suum in sinu tuo.	And direct the sick person to put their head in your lap. 
Deinde suspende illas uenas cum uncino uno, aut duobus secundum prudentiam tuam: et sit uncinus subtilis duplationis, secundum hanc formam, aut sint duo uncini gradat in corpore uno, secundum hanc formam.	Then suspend those good ones with one hook, or two according to your discretion; and let the hook be a fine one of double thickness, according to this form, or let there be two hooks joined together in one body, according to this form. 
Deinde collige cum forficibus subtilibus illas uenas cum subtilitate, et absterge sanguinem hora post horam, donec uideas illas uenas remoueri ex oculo, et resoluuntur: et caue ne laedas oculum cum extremitatibus spatumilis.	Then gather them carefully with fine forceps and wipe away the blood hour by hour until you see those veins receding from the eye and resolving; and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the speculum. 
Et sit operatio tua in meridie coram sole, et sis firmus in operatione tua ualde: ut non incidas nisi illas uenas.	Let your operation be in the middle of the day in front of the sun and be very firm in your operation so that you do not strike anything except those veins. 
Et cum tu expleueris, tunc distilla in oculum sief uiride, aut rubeum: ut sua acuitate corrodat quod remansit ex sebel.	And when you have finished, then distill green vitriol or red into the eye so that its sharpness may corrode what remains from the sebum.  
Si autem non est tibi possibile colligere illud totum in illa hora, tunc emplastra oculum cum eo, quod sedat dolorem oculi: et dimitte ipsum diebus aliquot, donec sedetur dolor eius: et securetur ab apostemate calido: deinde itera super ipsum secundum modum eundem, donec sanetur.	But if it is not possible for you to gather it all in that hour, then plaster the eye with something that soothes the eye's pain and leave it for several days until its pain subsides; and guard against a warm abscess; then repeat the process on it in the same way until it heals. 
Et haec est forma forficis.	And this is the form of the forceps.  
¶ De reductione Arissati ad nasum.	On the reduction of a nasal polyp.
Caput XIX.	Chapter 19.
Nominant medici Arissati Fistulam, quam curas cum cauterio, aut cum medicina acuta comburente, secundum quod praecessit eius narratio.	Physicians call a nasal polyp Fistula, which you should treat with a cautery or with an acute burning medicine according to its preceding description. 
Et si non sanatur, tunc non est ingenium in ea: nisi ut findas super apostema apud natiuitatem eius, et extrahas totam humiditatem quae est in eo et pus, donec detegatur os.	And if it does not heal then there is no skill in it except to cut above the abscess at its origin and extract all the moisture and pus from it until the opening is exposed. 
Cum ergo detegitur os, et uides in eo corruptionem, aut nigredinem, tunc rade ipsum cum instrumento, cuius forma est haec.	Therefore when the opening is exposed and you see corruption or blackness in it, then excise it with an instrument of this form. 
Et nominatur Asperi capitis.	And it is called Asperi Capitis.
Fiat ex ferro indo, et sit caput eius rotundum sicut azir, quod sit punctatum punctatione limae, aut punctatione aliskilferi punctatione subtili: et pone ipsum super locum corruptum ossis.	Let it be made of iron indo, and let its head be round like an azir, which should be punctuated with a file punctuation, or a subtle aliskilfer punctuation; and place it upon the corrupted place of the bone. 
Deinde reuolue ipsum inter digitos tuos, et tu preme manum tuam parumper, donec scias quod illa corruptio iam rasa est: et fac illud aliquotiens.	Then revolve it between your fingers, and press your hand upon it a little while, until you know that the corruption is already smooth; and do this several times. 
Deinde restaura locum cum medicinis exiccatiuis stipticis.	Then restore the place with drying astringent medicines. 
Si ergo consolidatur locus, et nascitur in eo caro, et abscinditur cursus saniei: et remanet quadraginta diebus, et non renouatur, et non apostematur, et non accidit in eo accidens: tunc scias quia iam sanatus est.	And if the place is consolidated and flesh arises therein, and the course of blood is cut off; and it remains for forty days, and is not renewed, nor does it fester, nor does any accident happen to it: then you will know that it is already healed. 
Et si non, tunc non est in eo ingenium, nisi reducere fistulam ad foramen nasi, secundum hanc formam.	And if not, there is no skill therein except to reduce the fistula to the nostril foramen, according to this manner. 
Et est, ut detegas ab osse secundo cum ferro, aut cum medicina acuta: et cum detectum est os, tunc accipe terebrum secundum hanc formam, sit extremitas ferrea, triangulata: et lignum eius sit pyramis extenuata usque ad extremitatem, sicut uides.	And it is, that you expose the second bone with iron, or with a sharp medicine; and when the bone has been exposed, then take an auger according to this manner, let its iron end be triangular; and let its wood be a pyramid tapered down to the extremity, as you see.  
Deinde pone illud super os ipsum: et sit illud prope lachrymale: et elonga manum tuam ab oculo parum.	Then place it upon the bone itself; and let it be near the lacrimal; and extend your hand a little from the eye.  
Deinde reuolue manum tuam cum terebro, donec penetret os, et sentiat illud infirmus: per hoc quod inuenit uentum exire ex eo, quando tenet manum suam super nasum suum.	Then revolve your hand with the auger until it penetrates the bone and feels weak; by this it finds wind escaping from it when holding his hand over his nose.  
Ergo tunc restaura locum cum medicinis stipticis exiccantibus, sicut docui te.	Therefore then restore the place with astringent drying medicines, as I taught you. 
Cum ergo nascitur caro, et induratur locus: tunc materia quae effundebatur ad exteriora, redit ad nasum: est ergo leuius illud super infirmum.	When flesh therefore arises, and the place hardens: then the material which was pouring out to the exterior returns to the nose; it is therefore lighter upon the weak one. 
¶ De reductione eminentiae Oculi.	On the Reduction of an Eye Eminence.  
Caput XX.	Chapter XX.
Quando eminet Oculus cum totalitate sua, et non accidit in uisu nocumentum, neque diminutio: tunc oportet ut soluas infirmum: deinde phlebotomes eum: postea ponas uentosas in ceruice absque scarificatione, sed cum suctione.	When an eye protrudes with its totality and neither harm nor diminution occurs to the vision; then it is necessary that you loosen the weak one; then phlebotomize him; afterwards apply cupping glasses to the neck without scarification but with suction. 
Deinde pone super Oculum linimentum quod fit ex acacia, et aloe, et olibano, et sarcocolla.	Then place upon the eye a liniment which is made from acacia, aloe, olibanum, and sarcocol. 
Deinde stringe Oculum desuper super emplastrum cum puluillis multis.	Then bind the eye above with a plaster and many poultices.  
Et modus puluillorum est: ut accipias pannos lenes, multos, et duplicetur omnis pannus ex eis super quatuor: fac ex eis multos: deinde pone eos unum super alium, secundum quantitatem qua indiget Oculus: deinde stringe super ipsos cum panno duro strictura forti.	And the manner of the poultices is: that you should take many soft cloths and double each cloth from them four times; make many from them; then place them one upon another, according to the quantity which the eye needs; then bind over them with a hard cloth a strong binding.  
Et itera uentosas cum suctione sine scarificatione.	And repeat cuppings with suction without scarification. 
Deinde aufer uentosas, et dimitte oculum strictum die et nocte.	Then remove the cuppings and let the eye remain bound day and night.  
Si autem ligamentum iterum mollificatur, tunc oportet ut stringatur multum: deinde aufer ligamentum post diem et noctem, sicut diximus.	But if the bandage again becomes loosened, then it is necessary that it should be bound tightly; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, as we have said. 
Si ergo uides oculum iam redisse uuae tunicae, est bonum: et si non, tunc itera emplastrum, et puluillos, et stricturam, et uentosas, donec sanetur.	Therefore if you see the eye has already returned to its former tunic, it is good; and if not, then repeat the plaster, poultices, binding, and cuppings until it heals. 
¶ De incisionie Vuae tunicae.	Concerning the incision of the tunics. 
Caput XXI.	Chapter XXI. 
Quando accidit disruptio in tunica Vuea, deinde eminet et procedit extra palpebras sicut granum Vuae, et foedatur forma hominis propter illud, et uis incidere illud: tunc operatio in eo est, secundum quod narro: et est, ut intromittas acum in radice Vuae ab inferiori ad superiorem partem.	When a rupture occurs in the tunic of the eye, and then it protrudes and proceeds beyond the eyelids like a grain of the eye, and disfigures the form of man because of it, and you wish to excise it; then the operation on this is as I shall relate: it is to insert a needle into the root of the eye from the lower to the upper part.  
Deinde intromitte acum aliam in qua sit filum duplum a parte lachrymalis, et fac eam penetrare: et dimitte acum primam secundum dispositionem suam.	Then insert another needle into which is a double thread from the lacrimal part and make it penetrate; and let the first needle go according to its own disposition.  
Deinde incide locum fili dupli, et liga cum eo partem Vuae in circumitu acus: et stringe eam multum.	Then cut the place of the double thread and tie it with the part of the eye around the needle; and bind it tightly. 
Deinde extrahe acum, et pone super oculum lanam infusam in albugine oui: et dimitte eum, donec cadat filum cum Vua.	Then extract the needle and place upon the eye wool soaked in egg white; and let it remain until the thread falls with the eye. 
Deinde cura oculum cum eo, quod confortat ipsum, donec sanetur uulnus.	Then care for the eye with that which strengthens it until the wound is healed. 
Et quandoque stringitur Vua ab omni parte cum circulo ex panno, donec addat oculus eminentiam magnam.	And sometimes it is bound by a circle of cloth from all sides, until the eye adds great prominence.  
Deinde perforetur cum spatumili subtili, quod perueniat ad profundum oculi, et currat humiditas albuginea, et descendat oculus, et ingrediatur statim: deinde stringe eum, donec sanetur.	Then pierce it with a fine speculum, which reaches the depth of the eye, and let the white humidity flow, and let the eye descend, and enter immediately; then bind it until it is healed. 
¶ De curatione Alcomnati.	On the treatment of Alconati. 
Caput XXII.	Chapter Twenty-Two. 
Haec Aegritudo quae nominatur Alcomnati, non, est nisi sanies, quae aggregatur in oculo, similis aquae descendenti, et non est ipsa.	This ailment which is called Alconati is nothing but blood which gathers in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not itself. 
Et modus operandi in ea est, ut facias sedere infirmum super sedem praeparatum, uel directum.	And the method of operation on it is that you make the weak person sit upon a prepared seat, or upright.  
Deinde accipe caput eius manibus tuis a partibus duabus, et moue ipsum, donec uideas saniem peruenire ad inferiora oculis tuis.	Then take his head with your hands on both sides and move it until you see the blood arrive at the lower parts of your eyes.  
Deinde figatur, et non descendat, et absoluatur lumen: et uideat infirmus res sicut uidebat: et si non descendit inferius, scias quia est aqua.	Then fix it so that it does not descend and illuminate the light; and let the weak person see things as he used to see; and if it does not descend below, you know that it is water. 
Si autem non praeparatur descensus saniei cum eo quod diximus, tunc fac sedere infirmum inter manus tuas.	But if the descent of the blood is not prepared with what we said, then make the weak person sit between your hands. 
Deinde accipe spatumile subtile, et finde cum eo supra panniculum corneum parumper apud continuationem coniunctiuae cum tunica cornea in corona, donec egrediatur sanies.	Then take a fine speculum and pierce with it above the corneal membrane a little at the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal tunic in the crown until the blood comes out.
Cum ergo egreditur, tunc distilla in oculum aquam calidam in qua miscuisti mel: aut aquam in qua iam bullisti foenumgraecum et mel: deinde curetur cum reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	Therefore, when it comes out, then distill into the eye warm water in which you have mixed honey; or water in which you have already boiled fenugreek and honey; then care for it with the remaining treatment until it is healed. 
¶ De cura aquae, quae descendit in oculo, uel cataracta.	On the treatment of water, which descends in the eye, or cataract. 
Caput XXIII.	Chapter Twenty-Three. 
Iam Diximus species aquae in diuisione, et quae conuenit ad perforandum sermone declarante et exponente, tunc accipe illud idem secundum sanitatem.	We have already said the kinds of water in division, and which is suitable for piercing by speech declaring and explaining, then take that same one according to health. 
Tunc ergo oportet ut facias sedere infirmum inter manus tuas quadratum, oppositum lumini, prope solem: et liga oculum eius sanum, et stringe eum ualde: deinde palpebram oculi eius manu tua dextra, si oculus in quo est aqua, est oculus sinister: aut manu tua sinistra, si oculus est dexter.	Then it is necessary that you make the weak person sit square between your hands, opposite the light, near the sun; and bind his sound eye, and constrict it strongly; then draw down the eyelid of his eye with your right hand, if the eye in which there is water is the left eye; or with your left hand, if the eye is the right one. 
Deinde accipe manu tua dextra almagda, si oculus est sinister: aut manu tua sinistra, si oculus est dexter.	Then take the lancet in your right hand, if the eye is the left one; or in your left hand, if the eye is the right one. 
Deinde pone extremitatem almagda prope coronam per grossitudinem radii in ipsa albedine oculi apparente lachrymalis minoris: deinde impelle almagda cum uirtute: et tu reuoluis cum eo manum tuam, donec penetret in albuginem oculi: et sentias, quod almagda iam peruenit ad rem uacuam.	Then place the point of the lancet near the cornea for the width of a radius in the very whiteness of the eye, appearing near the lesser lacrimal; then thrust the lancet with force; and you will revolve your hand with it until it penetrates into the albuginea of the eye; and feel that the lancet has now reached the empty thing. 
Et oportet, ut sit mensura itineris almagda ad profundum, mensura spacii quod est a pupilla usque ad finem nigredinis: et est corona oculi.	And it is necessary that the measure of the lancet's journey to its depth be the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye. 
Uidebis enim ea in ipsa pupilla uisione oculi, propter claritatem tunicae corneae.	For you will see these things in the very pupil by the vision of the eye, because of the clarity of the corneal tunic.
Deinde pone almagda usque ad locum in quo est aqua.	Then place the lancet up to the place where the water is. 
Deinde preme ipsum inferius uice una post aliam.	Then press it down below with force, one after another. 
Si ergo descendit aqua statim, tunc infirmus uidet illud super quod aperit uisum suum statim, et almagda in oculo suo.	If therefore the water descends immediately, then the weak person sees that upon which he opens his sight immediately, and the lancet in his eye. 
Deinde quiescas paululum.	Then rest a little while.  
Si ergo descendat aqua, tunc depone eam secundo, praeter quod egrediatur almagda.	If therefore the water descends, then deposit it a second time, beyond which the lancet goes out. 
Quando ergo figitur, et non ascendit: tunc extrahe almagda cum facilitate: et tu reuoluis manum tuam paulatim.	When therefore it is fixed and does not ascend; then extract the lancet easily; and you will revolve your hand gradually. 
Deinde dissolue in aqua aliquid ex sale claro gemmae: et ablue cum eo oculum deintus.	Then dissolve something of clear rock salt in water; and wash the eye within it. 
Deinde pone extra oculum totum stuppam, aut lanam infusam oleo rosato, et albugine oui: et liga cum eo oculum sanum.	Then place a whole cotton pad, or wool soaked in rose oil and albumen, outside the eye; and bind it with the sound eye. 
Nos autem, et illi qui sunt nostri temporis, ponimus super eum ciminum tritum cum albumine oui.	We, and those of our time, place ground cumin with egg white over it. 
Quod si non obedit tibi almagda ad introitum in oculum propter duriciem suam, quoniam ex hominibus est, cuius oculus est durus ualde: tunc oportet ut accipias spatumile, quod nominatur Alberid, cuius haec est forma.	But if the almond does not yield to entry into the eye because of its hardness, since it is from a man whose eye is very hard: then you must take a speculum called an Alberid, which has this form. 
Pefora ergo cum eo ipsam coniunctiuam tantum, et non ultimes manum tuam in foramine: et non est nisi ut facias uiam ad almagda locum subtilem.	Therefore pierce only the conjunctiva with it and do not insert your hand into the opening: and it is only so that you may make a way to the almond's place, which is narrow. 
Deinde intromitte almagda, secundum quod diximus.	Then introduce the almond as we said.  
Et apud complementum operis tui, praeparetur infirmo dormitorium decenter factum, in quo dormiat super dorsum suum in domo tenebrosa: et prohibeatur ab omnibus motibus, et a tussi: et pone cibum eius illud quo lenitur natura eius: et non moueat caput suum dextra, neque sinistra omnino.	And when your work is complete, prepare a well-made bedchamber for the weak one in which he may sleep on his back in a dark house; and prohibit him from all movements and coughing; and give him food which soothes his nature; and let him not move his head to the right nor to the left at all. 
Et sit ligamentum secundum dispositionem suam usque ad diem tertium.	Let the bandage remain according to its arrangement until the third day.  
Deinde solue illud in illa domo tenebrosa, et experire uisum eius: et fac eum uidere res.	Then loosen it in that dark house and make him try his sight; and have him look at things. 
Deinde reduc ligamentum usque ad diem septimum.	Then replace the bandage until the seventh day.  
Et non oportet ut faciat illud in hora curationis, aut post incisionem statim: imo oportet, ut alienes illud: propterea quod aqua ascendit uelociter per aspectum uehementem.	And it is not necessary that he do this during the hour of healing or immediately after the incision; rather, let others do it because water rises quickly through a violent gaze.  
Si autem accidit apostema calidum: tunc oportet ut soluas oculum ante septimum: et rectifica illud cum eo quod sedat apostema, donec sedatur: tunc absolue ipsius uisum, et pone super faciem eius orale quo regatur uisus eius sub eo diebus aliquot, ipso existente in illa domo tenebrosa.	But if a hot swelling occurs then you must loosen the eye before the seventh day and correct it with that which soothes the swelling until it is soothed; then release his sight and place an oral remedy on his face by which his vision is regulated for several days, he himself being in that dark house. 
Deinde egrediatur a domo gradatim, et conuersetur in casis suis.	Then let him gradually leave the house and engage in his usual activities.  
Et scias, quod in zaltea non excusatur discipulus a uisione aliquotiens: tunc enim audeat super operationem.	And know that a disciple is not excused from vision several times in surgery; then let him dare to perform the operation. 
Et iam quidem peruenit ad nos quidam ex illis qui sunt de Alayrach, qui dixit, quod factum fuit in Alayrach magdan perforatum, quo sugitur aqua.	And indeed, there has come to us a certain one from those who are of Al-Ayraq, who said that it was done in Al-Ayraq a perforated well, by which water is drawn up. 
Verum ergo non uidi aliquem in terra uostra, qui fecerit illud: neque legi illud in aliquo ex libris antiquorum: et est possibile, ut sit illud nouum.	But therefore I have not seen anyone in your land who has done that, nor have I read it in any of the ancient books, and it is possible that it is new. 
Et istae sunt formae specierum ex magda, ut stet super ea qui ea ignorat.	And these are the forms of species from a well, so that it stands upon it who does not know them. 
Fiant ex aere proprie: et sint extremitates eorum cum hac eadem subtilitate triangulatae, et extremitas acuta.	Let them be made of bronze properly: and let their ends be with the same delicate triangularity, and pointed end.  
Formae magda.	Forms of a well. 
¶ De cura Carnis natae in naso.	On the treatment of flesh born in the nose. 
Caput XXIIII.	Chapter XXIV. 
Quandoque nascuntur in naso Carnes diuersae additae, ex quibus est aliquid quod assimilatur scorpioni multorum pedum: et ex ea est caro cancerosa, lapidea, fusci coloris: et ex ea est quae est caro lenis, non fusci coloris.	Sometimes there are born in the nose various added fleshes, from which there is something that resembles a scorpion of many feet: and from it is cancerous flesh, stony, of a dark color: and from it is that which is soft flesh, not of a dark color.  
In ea ergo quae ex istis carnibus est lenis, non fraudulenta, neque cancerosa, oportet ut facias sedere infirmum inter manus tuas oppositum soli, et aperi nares eius, et proiice uncinum in illas carnes: deinde trahe eas ad exteriora, et incide quod comprehendisti ex eis cum spatumili subtili acuto a parte una, donec scias quod caro tota iam ablata est.	Therefore, in that which is soft flesh from these fleshes, not deceitful nor cancerous, it is necessary for you to make the infirm person sit between your hands opposite the sun, and open their nostrils, and project a hook into those fleshes: then draw them outward, and cut what you have grasped from them with a thin sharp scalpel on one side, until you know that all the flesh has now been removed.  
Quod si remaneret aliquid ex ea cuius abscisio non est possibilis: tunc rade illud cum uno instrumentorum subtilium cum facilitate, donec non remaneat ex eo aliquid.	And if something remained from it of which incision is not possible: then scrape that with one of the subtle instruments easily, until nothing remains from it.  
Si autem sanguis tibi dominatur, aut accidat apostema calidum: tunc oppone ei per id quod oportet: aut est ex apostematibus malignis, tunc propera cauterizando eum, donec abscindatur sanguis, et auferantur omnes carnes.	But if blood dominates you, or a hot abscess occurs: then oppose it by what is necessary: or if it is from malignant abscesses, then hurry to cauterize it until the blood is severed and all the flesh is removed. 
Deinde proiiciatur in nasum post incisionem acetum, et aqua, aut uinum.	Then vinegar, and water, or wine should be projected into the nose after the incision.  
Si autem aperitur nasus, et procedat ex eo humiditas usque ad palatum, tunc scias quia iam sanus est.	But if the nose is opened and moisture proceeds from it as far as the palate, then you know that it is already healthy. 
Si uero non penetrat humiditas, secundum quod oportet, tunc scias quod intra ipsum est caro nata in superioribus ossibus naris, ad quae non peruenit cum incisione instrumentum.	But if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you know that there is flesh grown inside it upon the upper bones of the nose, to which the instrument did not reach with the incision. 
Tunc ergo oportet, ut intromittas filum lini cui sit quaedam grossitudo, et noda in eo nodos multos: et pone inter omnem nodum quantitatem digiti, aut minus: et ingeniet infirmus, ut mittat extremitatem unam fili in nasum cum radio, aut cum quo possibile est ei postquam fecerit ipsum simile azer: et trahat odoratum suum, donec perueniat usque ad caassum, et egrediatur super guttur suum.	Then it is necessary that you introduce a linen thread which has some thickness, and knots in it many knots; and place between each knot the quantity of a finger, or less: and contrive, so that it sends one end of the thread into the nose with a rod, or with whatever is possible for him after he has made it like a razor; and draw out his odor, until it reaches as far as the palate, and emerges over his throat. 
Et multotiens quidem faciunt simile huic Attomi pueri in scholis: et est res facilis ei, qui uult.	And indeed very often they do something like this to children in schools; and it is an easy thing for him who wants to do it. 
Deinde pone duas extremitates fili, extremitatem unam quae egreditur super nasum, et alteram quae remansit in naso.	Then place the two ends of the thread, the one end which emerges over the nose and the other which remains inside the nose. 
Deinde ac ministra serraturam carnis cum nodis qui sunt in filo.	Then apply a flesh clamp with the knots that are on the thread.  
Fac illud donec scias quod carnes iam sunt cum nodis fili.	Do this until you know that the flesh is already held with the knots of the thread. 
Deinde extrahe filum: et pone in nasum post abstersionem sanguinis licinium quod imbibisti in unguento aegyptio: fac illud tribus diebus, aut plus, donec unguentum corrodat totum quod remansit ex carnibus.	Then draw out the thread and after removing the blood put a linen cloth soaked in Egyptian ointment into the nose; do this for three days, or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh. 
Deinde pone in fine rei in nasum cannulam de plumbo, diebus aliquot, donec sanetur.	Finally, at the end of the procedure, put a lead tube into the nose for several days until it heals. 
Si autem indiget curatione quae exiccet, utere illa.	But if it needs drying treatment, use that. 
Ad caputpurgium faciendum, cum quo distillantur olea, et aliae medicinae in nasum, fac illud ex argento, aut aere: quod sit simile lampadi paruae, apertum sicut conchula: et meatus eius similiter.	To make a nasal douche, with which oils and other medicines are distilled into the nose, make it from silver or bronze; which is like a small lamp, open like a shell; and its passageway similarly. 
Et si uis fac cannulam clausam, sicut canna.	And if you wish, make a closed tube, like a reed.
Et conchula instrumenti ad caputpurgium faciendum, sit plena, detecta: cui sit manubrium in postremo eius, cum quo teneas ipsam, quando calefacis in ea oleum, aut quod uis ex succis, et rebus fluxibilibus.	And the bowl of the instrument for making a head bandage should be full and open, with a handle at its end by which you hold it when heating oil or whatever juice or fluid substances you wish in it. 
Et haec est forma instrumenti.	And this is the form of the instrument. 
¶ De cura Thelul nasi.	On the treatment of a broken nose. 
Caput XXV.	Chapter Twenty-Five.  
Multotiens nascitur in extremitate nasi Thelul, et magnificatur, et augmentatur cum diebus, donec foedus fit aspectus eius.	Very often a break occurs at the end of the nose, and it swells and increases with each day until its appearance is ugly. 
Et propter illud oportet, ut in cidas illud in principio apparitionis eius, et eradices totum eius.	And for this reason it is necessary that you cut into it at the beginning of its appearance and remove all of it.  
Deinde pone super locum, aut cauterium, aut medicinam comburentem quae stat loco eius.	Then place upon the spot either a cautery or a burning medication which will stay in its place. 
Si ergo tardatur incisio eius, donec magnificetur, tunc considera, si est lapideum, durum, fusci coloris, pauci sensus: tunc non tangas ipsum cum ferro: quoniam apostema est cancerosum.	But if the incision is delayed until it swells, then consider if it is stony, hard, of a dark color, and has little sensation: then do not touch it with iron because it is a cancerous ulcer. 
Multotiens enim uidi, qui incidit hmoni apostema, et accidit ex eo malicia magna super illum qui ipsum habebat.	For I have often seen those who cut into such an ulcer and great harm befalls him who has it. 
Et si apostema est lenis tactus, non fusci coloris, et uides quod incisio possibilis est in toto eius, tunc euacua infirmum, et incide ipsum sine timore, absque pauore: et cura locum cum eo quod exiccat et constringit, donec sanetur.	And if the ulcer is soft to the touch, not dark in color, and you see that incision is possible throughout its entirety, then empty the weak spot and cut into it without fear or hesitation: and treat the area with something which dries and constricts it until it heals. 
¶ De sutura nasi, et labii, et auris.	On the suturing of the nose, lip, and ear.  
Caput XXVI.	Chapter Twenty-Six. 
Scias Quia quando accidit solutio continuitatis in una harum cartilaginum, parum confert in ea operatio, nisi in quibusdam hominibus.	Know that when a break occurs in the continuity of one of these cartilages, surgery makes little difference in it unless in certain people.  
Oportet ergo quando accidit alicui aliquid ex illo, ut consideres, si est uulnus recens cum sanguine suo: et tunc aggrega duolabia uulneris cum sutura: deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	Therefore when this happens to someone, consider if it is a fresh wound with its own blood: and then join the two lips of the wound with sutures; then treat it until it heals. 
Et si solutionis continuitatis labia iam separata sunt, et facta est unaquaeque pars sana: tunc oportet ut excories omnem partem a cute sua apparente, donec sanguinetur.	And if the lips of the break are already separated and each part has become healthy, then you must scrape away all the skin from its apparent surface until it bleeds. 
Deinde aggrega duo labia cum sutura, et stringe ea, et pulueriza super ipsum sanguinem draconis, et olibanum trita: et pone supra pulueres frustum emplastri diafinicon, et alicuius alterius ex emplastris consolidatiuis: et dimitte ipsum ligatum duobus diebus, aut tribus.	Then join two lips with suture, and tighten them, and sprinkle dragon's blood and ground frankincense upon it; and place a piece of diaphycon plaster, and one from another of the consolidating plasters, above the powders; and let it be tied for two days, or three. 
Deinde solue ipsum, et permuta medicinam: et dimitte ipsum, donec abscindantur fila per se.	Then untie it, and change the medicine; and let it be so until the threads are cut off by themselves.  
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento, donec sanetur.	Then care for it with ointment, until it is healed. 
Modus autem suturae est, ut aggreges solutionem continuitatis, aut cum acubus, sicut narrauimus in sutura uentris: aut aggrega solutionem cum filo, sicut feci te scire.	The method of suture, however, is to join the solution of continuity either with needles, as we have described in the suturing of the abdomen; or join the solution with thread, as I made you know.  
¶ De extractione nodorum labiorum.	On the Extraction of Nodes of the Lips. 
Caput XXVII.	Chapter XXVII. 
Multis Quidem hominibus accidunt plaerumque in interioribus labiorum suorum apostemata dura similia granis herbi: et quaedam eorum minora, et maiora.	Many men indeed have hard boils, similar to grains of herbs, occurring mostly in the inner parts of their lips; and some of these are smaller, and others larger. 
Ergo oportet ut conuertas labium, et findas super omnem nodum eius, et suspendas ipsum cum uncino, et incidas ipsum ab omni parte.	Therefore it is necessary that you turn the lip, and cut over all of its node, and suspend it with a hook, and incise it from every side. 
Deinde impleas locum post incisionem zegi trito, donec abscindatur sanguis.	Then fill the place after the incision with powdered zedoary, until the blood is cut off.  
Deinde colluatur cum aceto, et curetur locus cum eo, in quo est stipticitas, usquequo sanentur uulnera.	Then wash it with vinegar and care for the place with it, in which there is astringency, until the wounds are healed. 
¶ De incisione carnis natae super gingiuam.	On the Incision of Flesh Born Upon the Gum.  
Caput XXVIII.	Chapter XXVIII.
Multotiens nascitur super gingiuam caro addiat, quam antiqui nominant abuluss.	Very often flesh grows upon the gum, which the ancients call abuluss.  
Oportet ergo ut suspendas eam cum uncino: aut teneas eam cum forcipibus, et incidas eam apud radicem suam, et dimittas saniem currere, aut sanguinem.	Therefore it is necessary that you suspend it with a hook; or hold it with forceps, and incise it at its root, and let the serum run, or blood.
Deinde pone super locum zegi tritum, aut alios pulueres stipticos, exiccatiuos.	Then place powdered zedoary upon the place, or other astringent, drying powders.  
Quod si redit illa caro post curationem, nam multotiens redit, tunc incide eam secundo, et cauteriza ipsam: ipsa namque non redit post cauterium.	If that flesh returns after healing, for it often does, then cut into it a second time and cauterize it; for it will not return after cautery. 
¶ De rasione Dentium cum ferro.	On the reason of teeth with iron. 
Caput XXIX.	Chapter Twenty-Nine. 
Quandoque aggregantur in superficiebus Dentium ab interiori et extetiori parte, et inter gingiuas cortices asperi, turpes, et quandoque denigrantur, et citrini fiunt, et uirides, donec peruenit ex illo corruptio ad gingiuam, et foedi fiunt dentes per illud.	Sometimes rough, ugly crusts gather on the surfaces of teeth from both the inner and outer sides, and sometimes they become darkened, turning yellow or green, until corruption from that reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul through it. 
Oportet ergo ut facias sedere infirmum inter manus tuas, et caput eius in sinu tuo, et rade molam et dentem, in quo apparent tibi cortices, et res similis arenae: donec non remaneat ex eis aliquid, et similiter fac de nigredine, et uiriditate, et citrinitate, et aliis donec mundentur.	Therefore it is necessary that you make the weak person sit between your hands and their head in your lap, and grind a millstone and tooth, where crusts appear to you like sand, until nothing remains of them, and similarly do so with blackness, greenness, yellowness, and others, until they are cleansed. 
Si ergo auferatur quod in eis est a principio rasionis, bonum est: et si non, tunc itera super eos rasionem die alio, secundo, et tertio, donec ad ultimum perueniat studium in eo quod uis.	Therefore if what is from the beginning of the reason for them is taken away, it is good; and if not, then repeat the reason over them on another day, the second and third, until at last you achieve what you desire. 
Et scias, quod dens indiget rasoriis diuersarum formarum, multarum figurarum: secundum quod praeparatur operationi tuae: proptera, quod rasorium quo raditur dens ab inferiori parte, est aliud a rasorio quo raditur inter dentes, secundum formas alias.	And know that a tooth needs razors of various shapes and many figures according to how it is prepared for your operation; therefore the razor with which the tooth is scraped from the lower part is different from the razor with which it is scraped between the teeth, according to other shapes. 
Et istae formae rasoriorum sint apud te praeparatae, quas uides.	And these shapes of razors should be prepared by you, as you see.  
¶ De extractione doloris Dentium.	On the Extraction of Toothache. 
Caput XXX.	Chapter Thirty. 
Oportet ut cures Dentem a dolore suo cum omni ingenio, et tardes in eradicatione eius.	You must care for the tooth from its pain with all your ingenuity and delay in its eradication. 
Non est enim quod uicem eius suppleat quando eradicatur: quoniam est substantia sublimis: donec quando non est excusatio de eradicatione eius, tunc oportet quando cogitur infirmus eradicare ipsum, ut firmetur, et certificetur apud te dens dolens.	For there is no substitute for it when it is eradicated, as it is a noble substance: until when there is no excuse for its eradication, then when the weak person is forced to eradicate it, you must strengthen and assure yourself of the aching tooth.  
Multotiens enim decipit infirmum dolor, et putat quia est in dente saha et eradicat ipsum: deinde non recedit dolor, donec eradicetur dens infirmus.	Very often pain deceives the sick person, and they think it is in a sound tooth and extract it; then the pain does not cease until the diseased tooth is extracted. 
Nos enim iam uidimus illud ex operatione phlebotomatorum.	For we have already seen that from the operation of phlebotomists. 
Cum ergo certificatur apud te dens dolens ipsemet, tunc oportet ut scarifices in circumitu dentis cum spatumili, in quo sit quiddam uirtutis, donec soluatur gingiua ab omni parte: deinde moue ipsum digitis tuis, aut cum forcipibus subtilibus in primis paulatim, donec concutias ipsum.	Therefore when a painful tooth is confirmed with you, it is necessary that you make incisions around the tooth with a scalpel, in which there is some virtue, until the gum is loosened on all sides; then move it with your fingers, or with delicate forceps at first gradually, until you shake it. 
Deinde loca tunc in eo forcipes magnos locatione bona, et caput infirmi inter genua tua: quod iam bene tenuisti, ita quod non moueatur: deinde trahe dentem secundum rectitudinem, ut non frangas ipsum.	Then place large forceps in a good position on it, and the head of the diseased person between your knees: which you have now held well so that it does not move; then pull the tooth according to its straightness so as not to break it. 
Si ergo non egreditur, tunc accipe aliquod illorum instrumentorum, et intromitte ipsum sub eo ab omni parte cum facilitate, et conare motionem eius, sicut fecisti in primis.	But if it does not come out, then take one of those instruments and insert it under it from all sides with ease, and try to move it as you did at first. 
Si autem dens est perforatus, aut corrosus: tunc oportet ut impleas illud foramen panno: et stringas ipsum cum extremitate radii subtilis, ut non frangatur in hora constrictionis tuae super ipsum cum forcipibus.	But if the tooth is perforated or corroded, then you must fill that hole with cloth and tie it with the end of a fine ray, so that it does not break in the hour of your constriction upon it with forceps. 
Et oportet, ut exquisite agas cum scarificatione in circumitu gingiuae ab omni parte multum.	And you must act delicately with the incision all around the gum on every side a great deal.  
Et custodi fortitudinem tuam, ut non frangas ipsum, et remaneat pars eius, et redeat super infirmum ex ea malicia quae sit maior dolore eius primo.	And keep your strength, so that you do not break it, and a part of it remains, and returns upon the sick person from that greater evil which is his first pain.  
Et caue, ne facias illud quod ignorantes faciunt phlebotomatores in festinatione sua, et audacia ipsorum super eradicationem eius, praeter quod administrent illud quod narrauimus.	And beware, lest you do what ignorant phlebotomists do in their haste and boldness over its eradication, besides administering that which we have narrated. 
Multotiens enim faciunt euenire super homines infirmitates magnas, quarum difficiliores sunt ut frangantur, et remaneant radices eius omnes, aut quaedam earum: aut ut extrahant ipsum cum quibusdam ossibus mandibulae: sicut testificati sumus multotiens illud.	For they very often cause great infirmities to happen upon men, which are more difficult to break and which leave all or some of its roots remaining; or that they extract it with certain bones of the jawbone: as we have testified many times.  
Deinde colluatur post eradicationem eius cum uino, aut cum aceto et sale.	Then let it be washed after its removal with wine, or with vinegar and salt. 
Quod si accidat fluxus sanguinis ex locis (multotiens enim accidit) tunc tere aliquid ex zegi, et imple cum eo locum: et si non, cauteriza ipsum si non confert tibi zegi.	And if it should happen that there is a flow of blood from the places (for it often happens), then apply something from wool tow and fill the place with it: and if not, cauterize it if you do not have wool tow. 
Formae forcipum subtilium quibus mouetur dens in primis, sint longarum extremitatum, breuis manubrii, grossi, ut non duplicentur quando cum eis premitur super dentem: sint sicut uides grossorum manubriorum, donec quando stringis cum eis, non dent seipsas, neque duplicentur: breuium extremitatum, et sint ex ferro indo, aut ex faled decenter facti, directarum extremitatum: et in eorum extremitatibus sint dentes, quorum quidam ingrediantur in quosdam, et stringant constrictione decenti, forti.	The shapes of the forceps with which a tooth is moved should first be long-shafted, with a short handle, thick so that they do not double when pressed upon the tooth: let them be as you see with thick handles, so that when you squeeze them, they do not give way or double: with short shafts, and made of good iron or steel, well fashioned, straight-shafted: and on their ends are teeth, some which enter others and constrict with a decent force. 
Et quandoque fiunt extremitates sicut forma oris auis quae nominatur ciconia, et sunt fortis constrictionis.	And sometimes the ends are made like the shape of the mouth of a bird which is called a stork, and they are of strong constriction. 
¶ De eradicatione Dentium, et extractione ossium mandibularum fractorum.	On the removal of teeth, and the extraction of broken jawbones. 
Caput XXXI.	Chapter XXXI.
Quando remanet apud eradicationem Dentis qui frangitur aliquid, tunc oportet ut ponas super locum cotum cum butyro die uno, aut duobus diebus, donec mollificetur locus: deinde intromitte ad ipsum algasti, aut forcipes: quorum extremitates assimilantur ori auis quae nominatur ciconia.	When something remains at the removal of a tooth which is broken, then it is necessary that you put upon the place cotton with butter for one or two days until the place softens: then insert into it an algast, or forceps: whose ends are assimilated to the mouth of a bird called a stork. 
Forma autem haec est forcipum.	This is the shape of these forceps.
Sint extremitates eorum factae sicut lima deintus: aut sicut aliskilfegi.	Let their ends be made like a file within, or like a pair of pincers.
Si ergo non obedit tibi ad exitum cum istis forcipibus, tunc oportet, ut caues super radicem, et detegas carnem totam, et intromittas instrumentum quod nominatur Palanca parua, cuius forma est haec.	But if it does not yield to you towards its removal with these forceps, then it is necessary that you should carve upon the root, and detach all the flesh, and insert an instrument which is called a small Lever, whose shape is this. 
Sit breuis extremitatis, grossae parumper: et non sit imbibitum, ut non frangatur.	Let it be short-shafted, slightly thick: and let it not be imbrued so that it does not break. 
Si ergo egreditur radix per illud, est bonum: et si non, iuuare oportet cum istis instrumentis aliis quorum formae sunt istae.	Therefore, if the root comes out through that, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to pull with these other instruments whose forms are these. 
Forma primi triangulatae extremitatis, in qua est quaedam grossitudo.	The shape of the first one is triangular at the end, in which there is a certain thickness. 
Forma triangulatae extremitatis subtilis.	The shape of the triangular end is slender. 
Etiam iuuatur cum hoc instrumento habente duos ramos, cuius haec est forma.	It is also pulled with this instrument having two branches, which has this form.  
Et cum aliis instrumentis et ferramentis quae praecesserunt in rasione dentium.	And with other instruments and tools that preceded in the manner of teeth. 
Etiam sit iuuamentum cum hoc instrumento quod assimilatur uncino magno, huius formae, triangulatae extremitatis tortae, in qua est quiddam grossitudinis, ut non frangatur: et sit non imbibitum.	Pulling may also be done with this instrument which resembles a large hook, of this shape, with a twisted triangular end, in which there is some thickness so that it does not break; and let it not be soaked. 
Et scias, quod instrumenta dentium sunt multa: et similiter reliqua instrumenta non computantur, et artifex prudens, subtilis in arte sua inuenit per se ipsum instrumentum, secundum quod significant ei operatio et aegritudines ipsae.	And know that there are many tooth instruments; and likewise the other instruments are not counted, and a skillful artisan, subtle in his art, finds an instrument for himself according to what the operation and illnesses themselves indicate to him. 
Quoniam ex agritudinibus sunt ad quas non dixerunt antiqui instrumentum, propter diuersitatem specierum earum.	For there are illnesses for which the ancients did not mention an instrument because of the diversity of their kinds.  
Si autem frangatur os ex mandibula, aut ex aliis ossibus oris, aut putrefit: tunc perscrutare super ipsum in loco suo cum eo quod conuenit ei ex instrumentis et forcipibus quae dixi in extractione radicum, et iuuare cum gesti, cuius forma est haec.	But if the jawbone breaks from the mandible or from other bones of the mouth, or it putrifies: then carefully examine it in its place with what suits it from the instruments and forceps that I have mentioned in the extraction of roots, and pull with a pair of tongs, which has this form. 
Sit in eo quiddam grossitudinis paulatim, ut stringatur, uel teneatur cum eo os, et non fugiat et uadat, donec egrediatur os: et restaura locum cum medicinis conuenientibus ad illud.	Let there be a certain gradual thickness in it so that the bone is drawn tight or held with it, and does not flee and wander, until the bone comes out; and restore the place with suitable medicines for that.
Si autem in osse est putredo parua, tunc rade ipsum a putredine sua, et cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	But if there is a small putrefaction in the bone, then scrape it from its putrefaction and care for it until it heals. 
De serratura Dentium eminentium super alios.	Concerning the Lock of Teeth Projecting Above Others.
Caput XXXII.	Chapter Thirty-Two. 
Quando Dentes eminent non secundum cursum suum naturalem, foeda fit per illud forma: et praecipue quando accidit illud in mulieribus, et puellis, scilicet uenalibus.	When teeth project not according to their natural course, it becomes ugly through that; and especially when it happens in women and girls, namely those of marriageable age. 
Oportet ergo ut consideres.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to consider. 
Nam si dens est natus post dentem alium, et non locatur, uel est possibilis eius serratura, neque limatura ipsius: tunc eradica ipsum: et si est annexus cum dente alio, tunc incide ipsum cum isto instrumento, cuius haec est forma.	For if a tooth is born after another tooth and is not placed, or its serration is possible, nor its filing: then eradicate it; and if it is joined with another tooth, then cut it with this instrument, which has this shape. 
Est simile rostro paruo, et fit ex ferro indo, acutae extremitatis ualde.	It is similar to a small beak, and is made of tempered iron, with a very sharp end. 
Et sit incisio tua qua ipsum incidis in diebus multis, et propter duriciem dentis, et ut non commoueatur alius ex dentibus.	And let your incision be such that you cut it into many days, and on account of the hardness of the tooth, and so that another is not disturbed from the teeth. 
Si autem est eminens expositus limaturae suae: tunc lima ipsum cum lima ex indo, cuius forma est haec.	But if it is prominent and exposed to its filing, then file it with a file of tempered iron, which has this shape.  
Sit totum ex indo, et manubrium eius minutorum punctorum ualdae, sicut lima cum qua fiunt acus: cum quo limetur dens paulatim in diebus multis cum facilitate, ut non commoueatur dens, et cadat: deinde leni ipsum, in fine rade ipsum cum quibusdam rasoriis.	Let it be entirely of iron, and its handle of very small points, like a file with which needles are made; with which the tooth is filed gradually over many days with ease, so that the tooth is not disturbed, and falls out; then soften it, and in the end eradicate it with certain razors.  
Quod si est dens, ex quo frangatur pars, et laedit linguam: tunc oportet ut limes eum etiam, donec auferatur asperitas illius fractionis, et aequetur: et applanetur, et non laedat linguam, neque corrumpat sermonem.	But if there is a tooth from which a part breaks off and injures the tongue, then it is necessary for you to file it even until the roughness of that fracture is removed and it becomes equal; and it is made flat so that it does not injure the tongue nor corrupt speech.  
¶ De retatione Dentium cum filis auri.	Concerning the Retention of Teeth with Gold Threads. 
Caput XXXIII.	Chapter Thirty-Three.  
Quando accidit Dentibus anterioribus concussio et commotio a percussione, aut casu: et non potest infirmus stringere super illud quod comedit ut non cadat: et curasti eos cum medicinis stipticis, et non ualuit curatio: tunc ingenium in eis est, ut stringantur cum filo auri: quoniam argentum fit uiride, et putrefit post dies: sed aurum nunquam mutatur.	When the front teeth suffer a concussion and shock from a blow or fall, and the infirm person cannot bite down on it so that it does not fall out; and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and the cure has not worked; then there is an idea in this, for them to be tied with a gold thread; because silver turns green and rots after days: but gold never changes. 
Et sit filum medium in subtilitate et grossicie secundum quantitatem quod capiat inter Dentes.	And let the thread be medium in subtlety and thickness according to the amount that it takes between the teeth.  
Et forma quidem retationis est, ut accipias filum, et intromittas duplum eius inter duos dentes sanos: deinde texeas cum duabus extremitatibus fili inter dentes motos, siue unus sit, aut plures, donec peruenias cum tela usque ad dentem sanum alterius partis.	And indeed the manner of retention is to take a thread and insert twice its length between two sound teeth; then you weave with the two ends of the thread among the loose teeth, whether there be one or several, until you reach with the ligature up to a sound tooth on the other side. 
Deinde itera texturam usque ad partem a qua incaepisti: et stringe manum tuam cum subtilitate et sapientia, donec non remoueatur prorsus: et sit constrictio tua qua stringis filum, apud radices dentium, ut non euadat.	Then repeat the weaving back to the part from which you began; and tighten your hand with subtlety and wisdom until it is not at all moved; and let your constriction where you bind the thread be at the roots of the teeth so that it does not come loose. 
Deinde incide extremitates fili superfluentes cum forficibus: et aggrega utrumque, et conuerte eas cum gesti: et occulta ipsas inter dentem sanum et dentem motum, ut non laedat linguam: deinde dimittatur ita strictum dum remanet.	Then cut off the superfluous ends of the thread with forceps; and join both, and turn them over with a gesture; and hide them between a sound tooth and a loose tooth so that it does not injure the tongue; then let it remain thus tightened until it heals. 
Si autem soluitur, aut inciditur, stringe eos cum filo alio, et stabit cum eo taliter tempore toto.	But if they become loosened or broken, bind them with another thread and it will hold thus for the entire time.  
Et haec est forma Dentium, et figura retationis duorum dentium sanorum, et duorum dentium motorum, sicut uides.	And this is the form of Teeth, and the figure of retention of two sound teeth and two loose teeth as you see. 
Et quandoque fit, ut redeat dens unus, aut duo post casum urriusque in locis suis, et retentur sicut narrauimus, et remaneant: et non facit illud nisi artifex, prudens, et expertus.	And sometimes it happens that one or two teeth return to their places after a fall or blow, and are retained as we have described and remain; and this is not done except by a craftsman who is prudent and experienced. 
Et quandoque aptatur aliquod ex ossibus uaccinis: et fit ex eo sicut forma dentis, et ponitur in loco, ex quo munitur dens et stringitur, sicut diximus: et remanet, et seruitur cum eo tempore longo.	And sometimes a piece of bone is adapted; and it is made into the shape of a tooth, and placed in its place, from which the tooth is fortified and tightened, as we said; and it remains and is used with it for a long time. 
¶ De incisione ligamenti quod accidit sub lingua, et prohibet loquelam.	Concerning the incision of a ligament which occurs under the tongue and prevents speech.  
Caput XXXIIII.	Chapter XXXIV. 
Quandoque ligamentum hoc quod accidit sub lingua, est aut naturale, cum quo nascitur homo, aut accidentale, a uulnere quod iam consolidatum est.	Sometimes this ligament which occurs under the tongue is either natural, with which a person is born, or accidental, from a wound that has already healed. 
Et operatio in eo est, ut aperias os infirmi in capite eius in sinu tuo, et eleua linguam eius: deinde incide illud ligamentum neruosum per latitudinem, donec soluatur lingua a retentione sua.	And the operation on it is to open the mouth of the infirm person in your lap and raise their tongue; then cut that nervous ligament across its width until the tongue is freed from its restraint.
Quod si in eo fuerit quiddam duriciei et nodationis, et fuerit illud ex consolidatione uulneris: tunc proiice in illud uncinum, et finde illud per latitudinem, donec incidas ligamentum, et soluatur nodatio.	If there is something hard and knotted in it, and if that is from the consolidation of the wound, then thrust a hook into it and probe it across its width until you come upon a ligament and loosen the knot. 
Et caue, ne sit fissura in profundo carnis, et incidas arteriam illic, et accidat fluxus sanguinis.	And be careful that there is no fissure deep in the flesh so that you might cut into an artery and bleeding occur. 
Deinde colluatur in uestigio incisionis cum aqua rosata, aut cum aceto, aut aqua frigida.	Then wash the area of the incision with rose water or vinegar or cold water. 
Deinde pone sub lingua licinium ex lino, quod teneat infirmus in omni nocte: ut non consolidetur secundo.	Then place a linen wick under the tongue, which the patient should hold in his mouth all night so that it does not heal again.  
Si autem accidat fluxus sanguinis, tunc pone super locum zegi tritum.	But if bleeding occurs, then put powdered eggshells over the area. 
Si uero uincit te sanguis, tunc cauteriza locum cum cauterio lentiginoso, quod conuenit ad illud: deinde cura ipsum cum reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	But if the bleeding overcomes you, then cauterize the place with a lentil-shaped cautery which is suitable for that; and then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals. 
¶ De extractione Ranulae quae fit sub lingua.	On the Removal of a Ranula Which Occurs Under the Tongue. 
Caput XXXV.	Chapter Thirty-Five. 
Quandoque accidit sub lingua apostema quod assimilatur Ranae paruae, prohibens linguam ab operatione sua naturali: et fortasse magnificatur adeo, donec implet os.	Sometimes an abscess occurs under the tongue which resembles a small frog, preventing the tongue from its natural function; and perhaps it grows so large that it fills the mouth. 
Et operatio in eo est, ut aperias os infirmi coram sole: et considera apostema.	And the operation on it is to open the patient's mouth before the sun and examine the abscess.
Si ergo uides ipsum fusci coloris, aut nigri, durum, cui non inuenit infirmus sensum: tunc non tangas ipsum, quoniam est cancer.	And if you see it is of a dark or black color, hard, to which the patient does not feel sensation, then do not touch it because it is cancer.
Et si est decliue ad albedinem, in quo est humiditas, tunc proiice in ipsum uncinum, et incide ipsum cum spatumili subtili, et libera ipsum ab omni parte.	But if it is inclined toward whiteness and contains moisture, then thrust a hook into it and cut it with a fine scalpel and free it from every side.
Quod si uincit te sanguis in hora tuae operationis, tunc pone super ipsum zegi tritum, donec abscindatur sanguis: deinde redi ad operationem tuam, donec extrahas ipsum cum complemento eius.	But if bleeding overcomes you during your operation, then put powdered eggshells on it until the bleeding stops; and then return to your operation until you extract it with all of its contents.
Deinde colluatur cum aceto et sale: et cura ipsum reliqua curatione conueniente ad illud, donec sanetur.	Then it should be washed with vinegar and salt; and let it be cared for with other suitable treatment until it is healed. 
¶ De curatione apostematis duarum Amigdalarum.	On the Treatment of an Abscess in Two Tonsils.  
Caput XXXVI.	Chapter Thirty-Six. 
Quandoque accidunt inter guttur godad, id est, glandulae, quae similantur algodad, quae accidunt deforis: et nominantur duae Amigdalae: quas quando curas cum eo quod diximus in diuisione, et non sanantur, tunc considera.	Sometimes swellings occur between the throat and the palate, that is, glands which resemble almonds, and these are called two tonsils; when you treat them with what we said in the division, and they do not heal, then consider.  
Si ergo est apostema durum, fusci coloris, pauci sensus: tunc non tangas ipsum cum ferro.	Therefore if it is a firm abscess, dark in color, with little feeling; then do not touch it with iron. 
Et si est rubei coloris, et radix eius est grossa: tunc non tangas ipsum etiam cum ferro, timens fluxum sanguinis, imo dimitte ipsum, donec maturetur.	And if it is red in color and its root is thick; then do not touch it even with iron, fearing a flow of blood, but rather let it alone until it matures. 
Et tunc aut perforabis ipsum: aut rumpetur per se.	And then either pierce it or it will burst on its own. 
Et si est albi coloris, rotundum, et est radix eius subtilis: tunc oportet ipsum incidi.	And if it is white in color, round, and its root is slender; then it is necessary to cut it open.  
Et operatio in ipso est, ut consideres ante operationem suam, si quieuit apostema eius calidum quiete completum, aut imminuitur quadam diminutione: tunc ergo fac sedere infirmum coram sole, et caput eius sit in sinu tuo: et aperi os eius, et accipiat seruiens inter manus suas, et premat linguam eius inferius cum instrumento, cuius haec est forma.	And the operation on it is such that you should consider before your operation whether its hot abscess has quieted completely with rest or diminishes somewhat; then have the weak person sit facing the sun, and let their head be in your lap; open their mouth, and let a servant hold it between their hands and press their tongue down with an instrument which has this form. 
Fiat ex argento, aut aere, quod sit subtile sicut cultellus.	It should be made of silver or bronze, thin like a knife. 
Cum ergo premis cum eo linguam, et ostenditur tibi apostema, et cadit super ipsum uisus tuus: tunc accipe uncinum, et fige ipsum in amigdalam, et extrahe eam ad exteriora quantum potes, praeter quod trahas cum ea aliquid ex tunicis.	Therefore when you press it down with that, and the abscess is shown to you and your sight falls upon it; then take a hook and fix it in the tonsil, and draw it outward as much as you can, except that you pull some of the coats out with it. 
Deinde incide eam cum instrumento, cuius haec est forma quae sequitur.	Then cut it open with an instrument which has this following form.  
Assimilatur forficibus: uerumtamen extremitates eius sint curuatae, ita quod orificium cuiusque earum est in directo alterius acute: unde cura ut sit ex ferro indo, aut alfuled imbibitum.	It resembles forceps; nevertheless its tips should be curved so that the opening of each of them is directly in line with the other sharply; therefore take care that it is made of tempered steel or filled with alum.  
Si autem non est praesens hoc instrumentum, tunc incide ipsum cum spatumili, cuius haec est forma.	If this instrument is not present, then cut it with a scalpel, which has this shape. 
Sit acutum a parte una, non acutum a parte altera.	Let it be sharp on one side, not sharp on the other. 
Et postquam incidis amigdalam unam, incide alteram secundum hanc eandem speciem incisionis.	And after you cut one amygdala, cut the other according to this same kind of incision. 
Deinde post incisionem gargarizet infirmus cum aqua frigida, aut cum aceto et aqua.	Then after the incision, let the patient gargle with cold water, or with vinegar and water. 
Si autem accidat ei fluxus sanguinis, gargarizet cum aqua in qua bulliti sunt cortices granatorum: aut folia myrti, et similia illis ex stipticis, donec abscindatur fluxus sanguinis: deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	But if a flow of blood should occur, let him gargle with water in which pomegranate rinds have been boiled; or myrtle leaves, and things similar to these astringents, until the flow of blood is stopped; then care for it until it heals. 
Et quandoque nascuntur in gutture apostemata alia, praeter amigdalas duas.	And sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two amygdalae.  
Incide ergo ea secundum quod dixi in incisione duarum amigdalarum aequaliter.	Therefore cut them according to what I said in the cutting of the two amygdalae equally. 
Et ego quidem iam medicatus fui mulierem ex apostemate, quod natum erat inter guttur eius, quod trahebat ad fuscedinem, pauci sensus, quod iam fere clauserat guttur: et mulier respirabat a meatu stricto, et iam prohibuerat ei comestionem, et potum aquae: et iam peruenerat ad mortem, si remansisset uno die, aut duobus diebus.	And indeed I myself have already treated a woman from an abscess that had arisen between her throat, which was drawing it to choking, with few senses, because it had almost closed the throat; and the woman was breathing for me through a narrow passage, and had already prohibited her from eating and drinking water; and she had already come to death if she had remained for one day or two days. 
Et apostema tantum ascenderat, quod emiserat duos ramos, donec exierant super duo foramina nasi.	And the abscess had risen so much that it had sent out two branches until they came out above the two nostrils.  
Properaui ergo festinanter, et fixi in unum eorum uncinum.	Therefore I hurried quickly and fastened a hook into one of them. 
Deinde traxi ipsum, et tracta ex eo est portio magna.	Then I pulled it, and a large portion came out from it.  
Deinde abscidi eam, ubi comprehendi ex foramine nasi.	Then I cut it where I grasped it from the nostril. 
Deinde feci illud ei quod processit ex foramine nasi altero.	Then I did that to her which proceeded from the other nostril.
Deinde aperui os eius, et pressi linguam eius: et postea fixi uncinum in ipsum apostema: deinde abscidi ex eo partem eius, et non cucurrit ex eo nisi sanguis paucus: absolutum est ergo guttur mulieris, et incepit statim bibere aquam, deinde accepit ex cibo.	Then I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; and afterwards I fastened a hook into the abscess itself; then I cut off a portion of it, and there did not flow from it except a little blood; therefore her throat was cleared, and she immediately began to drink water, and then she received food. 
Non ergo cessaui incidere ex illo apostemate multotiens tempore longo: et apostema succedebat loco eius quod incidebam, donec prolongatum est nimis et cum ea illud.	Therefore I did not cease to cut from that abscess many times over a long period, and an abscess would succeed in the place where I cut it until it was prolonged too much and with it that. 
Ingeniaui ergo, et cauterizaui apostema inter guttur.	Therefore I devised and cauterized the abscess between the throat. 
Stetit ergo ab additione: deinde ambulaui a parte, et non sciui quid fecit Deus cum ea post me.	It therefore ceased from adding; then I walked away, and I did not know what God did with it after me. 
¶ De incisione apostematis uuulae.	Concerning the cutting of an abscess of the uvula.
Caput XXXVII.	Chapter Thirty-Seven.
Quando descendit catarrus ad uuulam, et apostematur, et est long: tunc ipsa nominatur perpendicularis: et si est in inferiori parte grossa, rotunda, tunc ipsa nominatur uua.	When a catarrh descends to the uvula and becomes abscessed and is long, then it is called perpendicular; and if it is in the lower part thick, round, then it is called uvula.  
Quando curatur cum eo quod diximus in diuisione, et non confert curatio: et uides quod apostema calidum quieuit ab ea, et est subtilis: tunc oportet ut incidas eam.	When it is treated with what we said in division, and the treatment does not avail; and you see that the hot abscess has ceased from it, and it is subtle; then it is necessary for you to cut into it.
Et quae ex ea est aggregata rotunda, et non est ei longitudo, et est sanguinea, aut fusci coloris, aut nigri, et non est ei sensus: tunc oportet ut deuites incisionem eius.	And whatever from it is a rounded mass, and there is no length to it, and it is bloody, or tawny colored, or black, and there is no sensation to it; then it is necessary for you to avoid cutting into it. 
In ea enim est timor super infirmum.	For in this there is fear over the weak one. 
Oportet ergo quando uides eam secundum modum quem dixi ex albedine, et longitudine sua, ut facias sedere infirmum coram sole: et premas linguam eius cum instrumento, cuius praecessit narratio: deinde fige uncinum in uuam, et trahe eam inferius: et incide eam cum uno duorum instrumentorum quae dixi in incisione duarum amigdalarum.	It is therefore necessary when you see it according to the manner which I said from its whiteness and its length, that you make the weak one sit before the sun; and press his tongue with the instrument of which we spoke previously; then fix a hook in the uvula and draw it downwards; and cut into it with one of the two instruments which I said in the cutting of the two tonsils. 
Et oportet ut non incidas ex ea, nisi illud quod additur super naturalem terminum sine additione.	And it is necessary that you not cut from it except that which is added above the natural limit without addition.  
Nam si tu incidis ex ea plus, laedes uocem et sermonem.	For if you cut from it more, you injure the voice and speech. 
Deinde post incisionem utere eo quod narrauimus in incisione duarum amigdalarum: et cura eam, donec sanetur.	Then after the cutting use what we narrated in the cutting of the two tonsils; and care for it until it heals. 
Si autem terretur infirmus ab incisione: tunc oportet ut utaris ingenio in cauterizatione eius absque timore et pauore.	If, however, the patient is terrified of the incision: then it is necessary for you to use skill in cauterizing him without fear or trembling. 
Et modus cauterii in ea non est, nisi cum aqua acuta: et est, ut ponas caput infirmi in sinu tuo.	And the manner of cautery in this is not done except with sharp water; and it is, that you place the head of the patient in your lap. 
Deinde preme linguam eius cum instrumento quod diximus.	Then press his tongue with the instrument which we have mentioned. 
Deinde accipe ex aqua quam dixi tibi in capitulo cauterizandi, et confice cum ea calcem non extinctam, et pone eam non spissam, neque subtilem, et imple ex ea concauitatem huius instrumenti, cuius haec est forma.	Then take from the water which I told you in the chapter on cautery and mix it with an unquenched lime, and put it neither thick nor thin; and fill the hollow of this instrument, which has this shape. 
Sit extremitati eius in qua ponitur medicina concauitas, sicut concauitas cochlearis radii.	Let the extremity in which the medicine is placed be a concavity, like the concavity of a snail's shell.  
Et pone instrumentum cum medicina super uuulam ipsam: et infirmus sit iacens super latus suum, ut currat saliua ex ore eius ex intrinseca medicina, ut non descendat ex ea ad guttur ipsius aliquid, et laedat ipsum.	And place the instrument with the medicine upon his tongue; and let the patient lie on his side so that saliva runs from his mouth through the inward medicine, so that nothing descends from it into his throat and harms him. 
Deinde tene manum tuam cum medicina.	Then hold your hand with the medicine.  
Et tu ex primas eam super uuulam quantitate medietatis horae, donec uideas eam iam denigratam, et sedatam mordicationem medicinae.	And you from the first place it upon his tongue for half an hour's time until you see it already blackened and the bite of the medicine quieted.  
Et si uis ut accipias cotum, et inuoluas ipsum super extremitatem radii, et infundas cotum cum medicina, et intromittas radium cum coto in cannulam desuper, donec adhaereat cotum super uuulam.	And if you wish to take cotton and wrap it over the extremity of the rod, and infuse the cotton with medicine and insert the rod with the cotton into the cannula from above until the cotton adheres upon the tongue.  
Fac illud multotiens, donec consequaris quod uis de cauterizatione uuae.	Do that many times until you achieve what you desire concerning the cautery of the vein. 
Deinde dimitte eam: ipsa namque arescit et cadit post tres dies, aut quatuor.	Then dismiss it; for it will dry up and fall off after three or four days.  
Quod si indiges ut iteres medicinam, itera ipsam: et post cauterizationem absterge in circumitu uuae cum coto imbibito in butyro, et mundifica cum eo quod est in circumitu eius ex medicina: et colluatur cum aqua frigida.	And if it is inconvenient for you to repeat the medicine, repeat it; and after cautery wash around the vein with cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse what is around it from the medicine; and gargle with cold water.  
Et curetur extrinsecus cum embrocis, et deintus cum gargarismis, donec sanetur.	And let it be treated externally with embrocations and internally with gargles until it is healed. 
Haec ergo species curationis est salubrior incisione et longinquior a timore.	Therefore this kind of treatment is healthier by cutting and farther from fear. 
Et quandoque curatur uuula etiam cum eo quod est subtilius quam cauterium et incisio: curatur enim cum suffumigatione, secundum hunc modum.	And sometimes a wound is healed even with something more subtle than cautery and incision; for it is healed with fumigation, in this way. 
Sume calamentum, et hyssopum, et origanum, et rutam, et sseah, et chamomillam, et abrotanum, et similia eis ex herbis: et aggrega ea omnia, aut quaedam eorum in olla, et submergantur cum aceto, et bulliant: et olla sit lutata cum luto decenter: et sit in medio ollae foramen, super quod componatur instrumentum concauum secundum hunc modum.
