Deinde compone quaedam eorum super quaedam cum figura quae sit in modo crucis: et liga cum eis alsifach, de quo diximus, quia est sub cute testiculorum ligamento uehementi, donec non possit aliquod ex uasis, quae nutriunt eos mittere ad eos aliquid: ut non accidat inde apostema calidum.	Then arrange some of them over some with a figure which is in the manner of a cross and tie them with the silk which we mentioned because it is under the skin of the testicles with a strong ligament until none of the vessels which nourish them can send anything to them so that a hot abscess does not occur from there. 
Et pone iterum ligamentum secundum extra ligamentum primum, longinquum ab eo minus duobus digitis.	And place again a second ligature outside the first ligature, distant from it by less than two fingers. 
Et post ista duo ligamenta dimitte ex sifach, quod est sub cute testiculorum, quantitatem magnitudinis digiti: et incide reliquum totum secundum rotunditatem, et aufer ex eo ouum.	And after these two ligatures dismiss from the silk which is under the skin of the testicles a quantity of the size of a finger and cut the remainder entirely according to its roundness and remove the testicle from it.
Deinde seca in inferiori parte cutis testiculorum sectione, ex qua currit sanguis, et sanies: sicut narrauimus in eo quod praemissum est.	Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles with a section from which blood and pus flow as we have related in what precedes. 
Deinde administra lanam submersam in oleo, et pone in uulnus: et administra ligamentum quod narrauimus.	Then administer wool soaked in oil and place it in the wound; and administer the ligature which we have related.
Et quandoque cauterizatur sifach album quod diximus, post incisionem eius timendo de fluxu sanguinis.	And sometimes the white silk which we mentioned is cauterized after its incision fearing the flow of blood.  
Multotiens enim accidit illud.	Very often it happens. 
Et dimitte ligamentum, donec cadat per se.	And release the ligature until it falls off by itself. 
Si autem tardatur casus eius, tunc embrocetur cum aqua calida: et pone super ipsum illud quod diximus, donec cadat.	But if its falling is delayed, then embrocate it with warm water and place that which we said upon it until it falls. 
Deinde cura uulnus cum reliqua curatione uulnerum, donec curetur.	Then care for the wound with the remaining care of wounds until it is healed. 
¶ De Ramice uentosa.	Concerning a windy branch.
Caput LXVI.	Chapter Sixty-six.
IN Hac Ramice non uidi aliquem qui ausus fuerit super curationem eius cum ferro.	In this branch I have not seen anyone who dared to treat it with iron. 
Et primi quidem dixerunt, quod fit sicut narrauimus in Ramice quae est cum Vite.	And first indeed they said that it is done as we narrated in the branch which is with a vine.
Quod est, ut liges uasa post sectionem super ea cum facilitate inferius: deinde seca in medio, et cura postremo cum eo quod aperit ipsum, donec cadant uasa: et cura uulnus, secundum quod diximus, donec sanetur.	Which is, to tie the vessels after section above them with ease below: then cut in the middle and finally care for it with that which opens it up until the vessels fall off: and care for the wound according to what we said until it heals. 
¶ De disruptione quae fit in inguinibus.	Concerning a disruption which occurs in the groins. 
Caput LXVII.	Chapter Sixty-seven.  
Quando accidit Ruptura in inguinibus, sicut diximus, et eminet locus, et non descendit ad testiculos aliquid ex intestinis: et si descendit, est illud parum, et redit in omnibus horis: uerum si prolongatur cum ea tempus, additur fissura in sifach, donec descendunt intestina in sifach.	When a rupture occurs in the groins as we said and the place protrudes and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it descends it is a little and returns in all hours: but if time prolongs with it, a fissure is added into the inguinal region until the intestines descend into the inguinal region.  
Et accidit illud ex extensione sifach, quod est in inguinibus, sicut diximus.	And this happens from the extension of the inguinal region which is in the groins as we said. 
Quod est, quia extenditur sifach: deinde mollificatur, et apostematur locus, et eminet.	Which is because the inguinal region is extended: then it softens and the place becomes inflamed and protrudes.  
Et cura eius est cum cauterio, sicut praecessit eius narratio.	And its care is with a cautery as its previous narration preceded. 
Et quandoque curatur cum ferro, secundum hunc modum: et est, ut iaceat infirmus super dorsum suum inter manus tuas.	And sometimes it is cared for with iron according to this manner: and it is that the sick person lies on their back between your hands.  
Deinde seca locum Rupturae apostematum et eminentem, sectione per latitudinem, secundum quantitatem trium digitorum.	Then cut the inflamed and protruding place of the rupture by a width according to the quantity of three fingers. 
Deinde stringe alsifak et, quae sunt sub cute, donec quando detegitur sifach album, quod est sub cute quae sequitur ipsum.	Then bind the ligature and what is under the skin until a white vein, which follows it, appears. 
Tunc accipe radium, et pone ipsum super locum eminentem ex sifach, et preme ipsum ad profundum uentris.	Then take a lancet and place it upon the prominent spot from the vein and press it deep into the abdomen. 
Deinde sue duo loca eminentia super extremitatem radii ex sifach, et annecte cum sutura unum eorum cum altero: deinde extrahe extremitatem radii.	Then make two prominent spots above the end of the lancet from the vein and join them together with a suture; then withdraw the end of the lancet. 
Et non incidas alsifach omnino, neque tendas ouum, neque aliud, sicut feci te scire in curatione ramicis intestinalis.	And do not cut the vein at all, nor strain the egg, nor anything else, as I have taught you in the treatment of a ruptured intestine. 
Deinde cura illud curatione uulnerum.	Then treat it with wound care. 
Cum ergo incidis fila, mundifica illud, et restaura uulnus, donec consolidetur.	When therefore you cut the threads, cleanse it and restore the wound until it consolidates.  
Sisach enim contrahitur, et non additur eminentia Rupturae.	For the vein will contract and no prominence of rupture will be added. 
Et cauterium est melius in hoc loco: quoniam est propinquius ad salutem.	And cautery is better in this place; for it is nearer to safety.  
¶ De mollificatione cutis testiculorum.	Concerning the softening of the skin of the testicles. 
Caput LXVIII.	Chapter LXVIII. 
Multotiens mollificatur cutis testiculorum in quibusdam hominibus, propter quod mollificantur carnes quae sunt inter ea, et foedatur aspectus eius.	Very often the skin of the testicles is softened in certain men, on account of which the flesh between them is softened and its appearance is marred. 
Ergo necesse est ei qui rogatur in curatione eius, ut faciat iacere infirmum super dorsum suum, et incidat totam cutem quae mollificata est super cutem naturalem.	Therefore it is necessary for him who is consulted in its treatment to make the sick man lie on his back and cut away all the softened skin upon the natural skin. 
Deinde aggreget duo labia cum sutura: et si uis, sue in primis superfluitatem cutis mollificatae tribus suturis, aut quatuor, et firma suturam.	Then he will bring together the two lips with a suture; and if you wish, first make three or four sutures on the excess softened skin and secure the sutures.  
Deinde incide inter sututuras.	Then cut between the sutures. 
Deinde cura curatione reliquorum uulnerum, usquequo sanetur, et cadant fila.	Then treat it with the care of other wounds until it is healed and the threads fall away.  
¶ De Castratione.	Concerning castration. 
Caput LXIX.	Chapter LXIX. 
Scias, quod Castratio in lege nostra excommunicata est: et propter illud liceret mihi, ut non rememorarer eius in libro meo isto: et non est necessaria rememoratio eius, nisi propter duos modos.	Know that castration is excommunicated in our law and for this reason it would be permissible for me not to remember it in this book of mine; and there is no need to recall it except for two reasons. 
Quorum unus est, ut sit illud in scientia medici quando interrogatur de ea: et ut sciat curationem eius cui accidit.	One of them is that it be in the knowledge of medicine when questioned about it, and that he know its cure to which it happens. 
Et modus alter est, quod nos multotiens indigemus castratione quorundam animalium, propter iuuamenta nostra per illud, sicut arietum, hyrcorum, et gattorum, et similium ex animalibus.	And another way is that we very often need the castration of certain animals for our benefits through it, such as rams, goats, and cats, and similar animals. 
Dico ergo, quod Castratio fit secundum duos modos.	Therefore I say that castration is done according to two methods. 
Aut per attritionem.	Or by abrasion. 
Aut per fissuram, et sectionem.	Or by fissure and incision. 
In illa autem quae fit per attritionem, uia operationis est: quod nos faciamus sedere animal in aqua calida, donec mollificentur testiculi eius, et leniantur, et pendeant: deinde attere eos manu tua, donec resoluantur et non appareant sub tactu.	But in that which is done by abrasion, the way of the operation is: that we make the animal sit in hot water until its testicles are softened and made pliable, and hang down; then rub them with your hand until they are resolved and do not appear to the touch. 
In castratione autem per fissuram et sectionem, oportet ut teneas animal, et premas cutem testiculorum eius cum manu sinistra.	But in castration by fissure and incision, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.  
Deinde liga suspensorium, et seca super omne ouum sectione una, donec quando procedunt duo oua: tunc incide ea postquam excoriaueris utrumque, et non dimittas super ea ex sifaket aliquid praeter sifac subtile, quod est super uasa.	Then tie the suspensory ligament and cut above the whole testicle with one incision until when two testicles proceed: then incise them after you have skinned both, and do not leave anything above them except a fine silk thread which is above the vessels. 
Et iste modus castrationis est melior eo qui fit per attritonem: quoniam attritio fortasse relinquit aliquid ex testiculis, quare desiderat animal coitum.	And this method of castration is better than that which is done by abrasion: because abrasion may perhaps leave something of the testicles, wherefore the animal desires copulation. 
Deinde cura uulnus, donec sanetur.	Then care for the wound until it heals.  
¶ De cura Hermafroditae duorum modorum.	Concerning the care of hermaphrodites in two ways. 
Caput LXX.	Chapter Seventy.
Hermafrodita ex uiris est secundum duos modos.	A hermaphrodite is from males according to two methods. 
Vnus eorum est, quia apparet in eo quod sequitur spacium, aut in cute testiculorum, in eo quod est inter duos testiculos, figura quasi uulua mulieris, in qua sunt pili: et quandoque currit urina ex eo quod est in cute testiculorum.	One of them is because it appears in it that there follows a space, or in the skin of the testicles, in that which is between the two testicles, a figure like a woman's vulva, in which there are hairs: and sometimes urine flows from that which is in the skin of the testicles. 
In mulieribus autem est species una, et est uulua mulieris super pectinem sicut testiculi uiri parui omnino, eminentes ad exteriora: quorum unus est sicut priapus uiri, et duo sicut duo testiculi.	In women there is one species, and it is the vulva of a woman above the pubic bone just like the testicles of a man small indeed, prominent externally: of which one is like the penis of a man, and two are like two testicles. 
Et curatio trium specierum, duarum ex uiris, et speciei unius ex mulieribus, est: quia oportet ut incidas carnes additas, donec effugiat impressio earum.	And the treatment of the three species, two from men and one species from women, is: because it is necessary that you cut away the added flesh until the impression of them escapes.  
Deinde cura eas curatione reliquorum uulnerum.	Then care for them with the treatment of other wounds. 
In specie autem secunda uirorum, ex qua egreditur urina, quae est in cute testiculorum, non est operatio, neque est eius curatio omnino.	But in the second species of men, from which urine flows out, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment at all. 
¶ De incisione Tentiginis, et carnis eminentis in uuluis mulierum.	On the Incision of a Tent-like Structure and Prominent Flesh in the Vulva of Women. 
Caput LXXI.	Chapter Seventy-One. 
Tentigo fortasse additur super rem naturalem, donec foedatur et turpis fit aspectus eius: et quandoque magnificatur in quibusdam mulieribus adeo, donec expanditur sicut in uiris, et peruenit usque ad coitum.	A tent-like structure perhaps is added on top of the natural part until its appearance becomes ugly and foul: and sometimes it magnifies in certain women so much that it expands like in men, and reaches as far as intercourse. 
Oportet ergo ut teneas superfluitatem Tentiginis manu, aut cum uncino, et incidas: et non ultimes in incisione, praecipue in profundo radicis: ut non accidat fluxus sanguinis.	Therefore it is necessary that you hold the excess of the tent-like structure with your hand, or with a hook, and cut it; and do not stop in the incision, especially in the depth of the root: so that bleeding does not occur. 
Deinde cura ipsam curatione uulnerum, donec sanetur.	Then care for it with the treatment of wounds until it heals. 
Caro autem orta, est caro quae nascitur in orificio matricis, donec impleat ipsum: et fortasse egreditur ad exteriora secundum similitudinem caudae: et propter illud quidam primi nominant aegritudinem caudatam.	But the flesh that arises is flesh which is born in the opening of the womb until it fills it; and perhaps it protrudes outwardly according to the likeness of a tail; and because of this, some of the ancients name the ailment tailed. 
Oportet ergo ut incidamus eam sicut incidimus Tentiginem, et curemus eam, donec sanetur.	Therefore it is necessary that we cut it just as we cut the tent-like structure, and care for it until it heals.  
¶ De cura Alratica, quae est uulua mulieris non perforata.	On the Treatment of Atresia, Which Is an Imperforate Vulva. 
Caput LXXII.	Chapter Seventy-Two. 
Alratica est, ut sit uulua mulieris non perforata, aut sit foramen paruum.	Atresia is when the vulva of a woman is not perforated, or when there is a small opening.  
Et est aut naturalis, aut accidentalis.	And it is either natural or accidental. 
Accidentalis est ex aegritudine quae praecessit: et ipsa quidem fit aut ex carne nata addita, aut sifach subtili, aut spisso: et fit aut in profundo matricis, aut in lateribus eius, aut in superiore ipsius, aut inferiori eius: et prohibet a coitu et impregnatione, et partu, et fortasse prohibet menstrua.	It is accidental from a preceding illness and it indeed arises either from added flesh, or a thin or thick ulcer and it occurs either in the depth of the matrix, or on its sides, or on its upper part, or its lower part; and it prevents coitus, impregnation, childbirth and perhaps menstruation. 
Et cognitio illius fit per aspectum obstetricis, si opilatio est apparens propinqua.	And recognition of it is made by the midwife's inspection if the suture is an apparent approach.  
Si autem non est apparens, tunc quaere eam digitis tuis, aut cum radio.	But if it is not apparent then seek it with your fingers or a probe. 
Si autem opilatio est ex sifach subtili, et est propinqua duobus labiis: tunc propera, et disrumpe ipsam.	But if the suture is from a thin ulcer and is near both lips then hasten and disrupt it. 
Et est, ut ponas super duo labia puluillos.	And it is necessary to place poultices upon the two lips.  
Deinde pone indices tuos duarum manuum simul, et mulier sit super dorsum suum expansis cruribus suis.	Then place the index fingers of both your hands together and let the woman be on her back with her legs spread. 
Deinde extende duo labia cum fortitudine, donec disrumpatur sifach subtile, et aperiatur opilatio.	Then extend the two lips with force until the thin ulcer is disrupted and the suture is opened.  
Deinde accipe lanam, et imbibe eam in oleo, et pone ipsam super locum: et coeat mulier omni die, ut non consolidetur locus uice alia.	Then take wool and soak it in oil and place it upon the spot, and let the woman come every day so that the place does not consolidate with other fluids.  
Si autem sifach est grossum, spissum: tunc oportet ut seces ipsum cum spatumili lato simili folio myrti.	But if the ulcer is large and thick then it is necessary to cut it out with a broad spatula like a myrtle leaf.  
Si autem opilatio est ex carne nata, tunc suspende eam cum uncinis, et incide eam: et sint tecum medicinae quae fluxum sedant sanguinis absque mordicatione, sicut acacia, et sanguis draconis, et thus aggregatum cum albugine oui.	But if the suture is from added flesh then suspend it with hooks and cut into it and have with you medications which stop the flow of blood without biting such as acacia, dragon's blood, and litharge mixed with albumen. 
Deinde administra cannulam ex plumbo amplam, ut non consolidetur uulnus uelociter, teneat eam diebus aliquot: et administra licinium ex lino sicco, deinde curetur reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	Then insert a wide lead cannula so that the wound does not consolidate quickly, and hold it for several days; then administer linen cerate from dry flax, and then let the rest be cared for until it is healed.  
Et quandoque nasciur in matrice natiuitas carnium aliarum: oportet ergo ut incidantur secundum hunc modum: dum non est apostema cancerosum apostemati enim canceroso quod est in matrice, non fiat contrarietas cum ferro omnino.	And sometimes other flesh growths are born within the matrix; therefore it is necessary that they be cut according to this method: but if there is a cancerous abscess then an abscess which is cancerous within the matrix should not at all be opposed with iron. 
¶ De cura hemorroidarum, Athehelil, et Bothor rubeae in uuluis mulierum.	On the treatment of hemorrhoids, Athehelil and Bothor rubeae in the vulvas of women. 
Caput LXXIII.	Chapter Seventy-Three. 
Hemorroides quidem sunt apertio orificiorum uenarum, donec currit ex eis sanguis multus assidue.	Hemorrhoids are indeed the open orifices of veins, from which much blood constantly flows. 
Cum ergo antiquantur hemorroides, fiunt thelil: et iam dixi in diuisione species earum, et signa ipsarum: et dicam hic quae ex eis recipiunt curationem, et quae non.	Therefore when hemorrhoids become ancient they become thelil and as I have already said in the division of their kinds and signs, I will say here which receive cure from them and which do not. 
Dico ergo, quod hemorroides quae sunt in orificio matricis, et non apparent sensui: tunc non est ei curatio cum ferro.	I therefore say that hemorrhoids which are in the orifice of the uterus and do not appear to the sense, then there is no cure for them with iron. 
Quae autem ex eis sunt in orificio matricis super quas cadit sensus, sunt quae curantur.	Those however which are from them in the orifice of the uterus on which sense falls are those that are cured.  
Oportet ergo ut intromittas mulierem in domum frigidam.	It is necessary therefore that you introduce the woman into a cold house. 
Deinde extende athehelil cum forficibus, aut cum panno aspero, et incide eas ex radicibus suis.	Then extend the athehelil with forceps or with a rough cloth and cut them out from their roots. 
Deinde pulueriza super eas apud fluxum sanguinis ex uno puluerum incisiuorum absque mordificatione: sicut acacia, et sanguis draconis, et thus, et similia eis.	Then powder over them at the flow of blood from one of the cutting powders without modification: such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and thus, and those similar to them. 
Deinde impellat pedes eius ad parietem hora una.	Then press her feet against the wall for one hour.
Postea depone eam in aquam frigidam.	Afterwards place her in cold water. 
Quod si perseuerat fluxus sanguinis: tunc fac eam sedere in decoctione sumach, et corticum granatorum, et gallarum, et similium.	And if the flow of blood persists then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, and pomegranate rinds, and galls, and similar things.
Deinde accipe farinam hordei, et confice eam cum melle et aceto, et fac emplastrum cum eo super dorsum eius.	Then take barley flour and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on her back. 
Si ergo abscinditur sanguis cum eo, bonum est: et si non, fac adhaerere dorso uentosas, et mammillis, absque scarificatione.	If therefore the blood is cut off with it, it is good and if not, make the windy ones adhere to the back and breasts without scarification.
Deinde accipe lanam, et submerge in succo tarathit, aut succo arnoglossae, aut succo ramorum alaulat, id est, aglanter, uino pontico, et fac adhaerere loeo.	Then take wool and submerge it in the juice of tarathit or the juice of arnoglossa or the juice of the branches of alaula which is aglanter, Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the place. 
Cum ergo quiescit apostema, tunc cura locum cum unguentis, donec sanetur.	Therefore, when the abscess is quiet, care for the place with ointments until it heals. 
Albarth uero rubeum est simile capitibus alhaasse, et est asperi aspectus.	But albarth is reddish and similar to the heads of alfalfa, and has a rough appearance. 
Oportet ergo ut incidas quod apparet ex eo, secundum quod dixi in thelil aequaliter: et cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	Therefore it is necessary that you cut out what appears from it, according to what I said in the chapter equally; and care for it until it heals. 
¶ De perforatione Exiturae quae accidit in matrice.	Concerning the Perforation of a Fistula Which Occurs in the Womb. 
Caput LXXIIII.	Chapter Seventy-Four.
Accidunt in matrice species multae apostematum, sicut cancer, et apostema lapideum, et ulcera, et adubelati, et alekilati, id est, herpes, aestiomemus, et fistulae, et hemorroides, et ragadiae, et thelil, et apostema calidum.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the womb, such as cancer, and stony abscess, and ulcers, and adubelati, and alekilati, that is herpes, aestiomemus, and fistulas, and hemorrhoids, and fissures, and thelil, and hot abscess.  
Et ego quidem iam dixi omnes has aegritudines et species earum, et signa ipsarum, et earum curationes in diuisione: necesse est ut dicam in hoc tractatu apostema calidum quod accidit in matrice, quando est ex apostematibus quae colligunt saniem, et uis scire qualiter fit eius apertio cum ferro.	And I have indeed already said all these diseases and their kinds, and their signs, and their treatments in the division: it is necessary that I say in this treatise about a hot abscess which occurs in the womb, when it is from abscesses which collect pus, and you wish to know how its opening is made with an iron instrument.  
Oportet ergo ut consideres.	Therefore it is necessary that you consider. 
Tunc si dolor apostematis in incaeptione sua est acutus cum percussione sua, et flamma, et febre: et uides ipsum rubere: si cadit super ipsum sensus, tunc non properes cum perforatione eius: et cura ipsum cum eo eo quod iuuat super maturationem, donec quando quiescat acuitas accidentium.	Then if the pain of the abscess in its beginning is sharp with percussion, and burning, and fever; and you see it reddening; if numbness falls upon it, then do not hurry with its perforation; and care for it with that which helps with its maturation, until when the sharpness of the accidents subsides. 
Tunc oportet ut facias sedere mulierem super sedem quae labeat duo sedilia, et reclinetur, uel appodietur super dorsum suum, et aggreget pedes suos ad partem inferiorem uentris: et sint coxae eius expansae, et ponat brachia sua sub genibus suis, et liget utraque ligamento conueniente ad illud.	Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit upon a seat which beats two seats, and recline, or lean upon her back, and gather her feet to the lower part of her belly; and let her hips be spread, and put her arms under her knees, and bind each one with a suitable ligament to it. 
Deinde sedeat obstetrix a latere dextro, et administra instrumentum quo aperitur orificium matricis.	Then let the midwife sit from her right side, and administer the instrument by which the opening of the womb is opened.  
Cuius forma uenit in eis quae sunt post.	Whose shape comes in those which are behind. 
Et oportet quando uis administrare hoc instrumentum, ut figas cum Radio profundum matricis mulieris: ut non sit illud quod ingreditur ex instrumento plus, quam profundum matricis, et laedat infirmam.	And it is necessary when you wish to administer this instrument, that you fix it with the Speculum deep in the matrix of the woman: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the matrix, and injures the delicate parts.  
Si autem fuerit instrumentum magis quam profundum, tunc oportet ut ponas puluillos super tecturam profundi matricis: ut prohibeatur introitus instrumenti totius in profundum matricis: et oportet ut ponat uertiginem, quae currit in instrumento, ex latere superiore: et ut teneat instrumentum, et ut reuoluat minister uertiginem, donec aperiatur profundum matricis.	But if the instrument is more than deep, then it is necessary that you place pledgets upon the covering of the deep matrix: so that entry of the whole instrument into the depth of the matrix is prohibited: and it is necessary that you place a knob, which runs in the instrument, from its upper side: and that you hold the instrument, and that the attendant turns the knob until the deep matrix is opened.  
Cum ergo apparet Exitura, et tangitur manu, et est lenis et mollis: tunc oportet ut seces ipsam apud caput suum cum spatumili lato.	Therefore when the Cervix appears and is touched by the hand, and it is soft and pliable: then it is necessary that you cut it at its head with a broad spatula. 
Cum ergo euacuatur sanies, tunc oportet ut ponas in uulnus licinium submersum in oleo rosaceo: aut oleo uiridi, in quo sit quaedam stipticitas: et pone licinium, et extrahe sectionem in profundo matricis.	Therefore when the blood is evacuated, then it is necessary that you place a linen cloth steeped in rose oil or green oil, in which there is some astringency: and place the linen cloth, and draw out the incision into the depth of the matrix.  
Et pone exterius super matricem, et super pectinem lanam mundam submersam in aqua, in qua bullitae sunt maluae.	And place externally upon the matrix, and upon the comb clean wool steeped in water, in which apples have been boiled. 
Deinde curetur post duos dies cum unguento quod conuenit ad illud, donec sanetur.	Then let it be cared for after two days with ointment which suits it, until it is healed.  
Et quandoque abluitur matrix et uulnus, ita quod clisterizatur cum aqua et melle: deinde cum aqua in qua bullita est radix lilii, aut aristolochia longa: deinde redeat ad unguentum.	And sometimes the matrix and wound are washed, so that it is cleansed with water and honey: then with water in which the root of a lily or long birthwort has been boiled: then return to ointment. 
Quod si uulnus absconditum fuerit interius in matrice, tunc oportet ut prohibearis ex curatione eius cum ferro, imo cura ipsum cum eo quod diximus in diuisione.	But if the wound is hidden interiorly within the matrix, then it is necessary that you withhold from its treatment with iron, but rather treat it with what we said in the division. 
¶ Doctrinae Obstetricum, qualiter medicentur embriones uiui, secundum figuram non naturalem egressi.	Doctrine of Obstetrics, how living embryos are treated, according to a figure not natural.  
Caput Lxxu.	Chapter LXXV. 
Necesse est Obstetrici, ut cognoscat in primis figuram partus naturalis.	It is necessary for a midwife to know first the form of natural childbirth. 
Ex signis ergo eius est, quod quando uides mulierem comprimi ad inferiora, et desiderat odorare aerem, et alleuiatur super eam quod super ipsam est de partu, et festinat exitus embrionis: tunc scias quod iste partus est secundum figuram naturalem, et est exitus eius super caput suum, et secundina cum eo: aut suspensa, uel pendens ex umbilico.	Therefore, from these signs it is so that when you see a woman pressing down towards her lower parts, and she desires to smell the air, and relief comes over her about the matter of childbirth upon her, and she hastens the exit of the embryo: then you know that this childbirth is according to the natural form, and its exit is upon its head, and secondarily with it; or suspended, or hanging from the umbilical cord. 
Cum ergo uides haec signa, tunc oportet ut comprimatur uenter eius, ut descendat embrio uelociter.	Therefore when you see these signs, it is necessary that her belly be compressed so that the embryo descends quickly.  
Nam quando descendit super caput suum, descendit secundina cum eo, et mundatur ex illis superfluitatibus mundificatione bona.	For when it descends upon its head, the second child descends with it, and it is cleansed from those superfluities by a good cleansing. 
Qui autem est praeter hunc partum, est innaturalis, illaudabilis.	But that which is besides this childbirth is unnatural, undesirable. 
Quoniam quandoque egreditur foetus super pedes suos, et egreditur corpus eius ante caput ipsius, et pedes eius, et manus eius una, aut pes eius unus: aut egreditur caput eius et manus eius: aut egreditur uentrinus: et fortasse conuertitur super collum suum, et similia ex figuris illaudabilibus.	For sometimes the fetus exits upon its feet, and its body exits before its head, and its feet and hands together, or one of its feet; or its head and hands exit; or its belly exits; and perhaps it turns upon its neck, and similar undesirable figures.  
Necesse est ergo Obstetrici, ut sit prudens, subtilis in istis rebus omnibus, et caueat sibi ab errore et decaeptione: et ego sum ostendens omnem figuram ex eis, et qualiter est ingenium in ea, et significetur per illud, et stetur super ipsum.	Therefore it is necessary for a midwife to be prudent, subtle in all these matters, and to beware of error and deception: and I am showing every figure from them, and how its nature is in it, and let it be signified by that, and let it stand upon it. 
Quando egreditur foetus super caput suum egressione sua naturali, et uehemens fit illud super mulierem, et difficilis fit ei partus, et uides uirtutem eius iam debilitatam: tunc fac eam sedere super sedem, aut mulieres teneant eam: et uapora uuluam eius cum foenugraeco decocto, et cum oleis humidis.	When the fetus exits upon its head in its natural exit, and it becomes vehement upon the woman, and childbirth becomes difficult for her, and you see her strength already weakened; then make her sit upon a seat, or let women hold her; and apply vapors to her vulva with decocted fenugreek, and with moist oils.  
Deinde intromittat Obstetrix inter digitos suos Spatumile paruum, et findat cum eo secundinam, et secet eam ungue suo, donec currat quod est in ea ex humiditate: et preme uentrem mulieris, donec descendat foetus.	Then let the midwife insert a small spatula between her fingers, and bind it with the second child, and cut it with her fingernail until what is in it runs out from moisture; and press the woman's belly until the fetus descends. 
Si autem non descendit, tunc oportet ut clisterizetur mulier ex mucillagine foenugraeci, cum oleo sisamino.	If it does not descend, then she must be given an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesamum oil. 
Deinde praecipe ei post clistere, ut comprimatur: et fac eam sternutare cum condisi, et tene os eius et nasum ipsius hora una.	Then order her after the enema to be compressed; and make her snore while she is being compressed, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. 
Foetus enim egredietur statim.	For the fetus will immediately come out. 
Quod si egrediantur duae manus foetus in primis, iunc oportet ut reducas eas cum facilitate paulatim.	But if two hands of the fetus emerge first, it is necessary that you reduce them gradually with ease. 
Si autem non obedit in introitu, tunc pone mulierem super sedem, et eleua pedes eius sursum: deinde concute sedem super terram: et mulier teneatur, ut non cadat apud concussionem.	But if it does not obey upon entering, then place the woman on a seat and elevate her feet upward; then strike the seat upon the ground; and let the woman be held so that she does not fall during the impact. 
Si ergo non egrediuntur manus, et moritur foetus: tunc incide eas, et extrahe residuum foetus: et liga manum eius cum panno, et extrahe ipsum cum aequalitate: nam ipse egredietur.	But if the hands do not emerge and the fetus dies, then cut them open and extract the remaining fetus; and tie his hand with a cloth and pull it out evenly, for it will come out itself. 
¶ Exitus embrionis super pedes suo.	The delivery of an embryo on its feet.
Quando egreditur foetus super pedes suos, tunc oportet ut impellat eos sursum: deinde conuertat foetum paulatim: postea aequet ipsum.	When the fetus comes out on its feet, then it is necessary to push them upward; then turn the fetus gradually; afterwards equalize it. 
Deinde accipiat unum pedum eius, et extendat eum paulatim.	Then let him take hold of one of its feet and extend it gradually.  
Cum ergo egrediuntur usque ad coxas, tunc praecipe ei, ut comprimatur, et fac eam sternutare cum condisi: egredietur enim, si Deus uoluerit.	When they emerge up to the hips, then order her to be compressed and make her snore while she is being compressed; for it will come out if God wills. 
Et si non egreditur cum eo quod narrauimus, tunc reduc foetum paulatim, donec ponas eum secundum figuram naturalem.	And if it does not come out with what we have related, then reduce the fetus gradually until you place it according to its natural form.  
Nam ipse egredietur tunc egressu facili.	For it will then come out with an easy delivery. 
Quod si prohibeatur cum eo toto quod narrauimus: tunc accipe ex mucillagine alteae, et oleo sisamino, et gummi soluto: et percute totum in mortario percussione bona: deinde line cum eo uuluam mulieris, et inferius uentris eius.	But if it is hindered with all that we have related, then take fenugreek mucilage and sesamum oil, and dissolved gum; and strike the whole in a mortar with good percussion; then mix it with the vulva of the woman and below her belly. 
Deinde fac eam sedere in aqua tepida, donec consequatur hypocundria.	Then have her sit in warm water until the hypocondrium is reached. 
Cum ergo uides quod iam calefacta sunt inferiora eius, tunc fac ei sief de myrrha: et suppone ipsum.	When therefore you see that her lower parts are already heated, then give her a suppository of myrrh and insert it.  
Quando ergo tenet sief hora una, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem.	When therefore she has held the suppository for an hour, then have her sit upon a seat. 
Deinde fac eam sternutare: et stringe ipsius os et nasum: et preme inferiorem partem uentris compressione facili.	Then have her strain; and bind her mouth and nose; and press the lower part of the belly with a gentle compression.  
Nam foeus egredietur statim.	For the fetus will immediately come out. 
¶ Exitus foetus super genua et manus.	The exit of the fetus over the knees and hands.
Quando egreditur secundum hanc formam, tunc ingeniet in intromittendo manus suas paulatim.	When it exits according to this form, then begin gently inserting your hands. 
Deinde resupinetur mulier super collum suum, et pendeant pedes eius ad inferiora: et ipsa sit iacens super lectum, et complicet manus suas.	Then the woman is turned onto her neck, and her feet hang down to the lower part; and she lies upon the bed, and folds her hands. 
Deinde preme supra uentrem eius paulatim.	Then press upon her belly gently.  
Deinde extrahe quod est sub pedibus eius ex puluinaribus, donec sit praeparata in inferiori parte.	Then extract what is under her feet from the pillows until it is prepared in the lower part. 
Quod si non egreditur foetus, tunc accipe pedes eius, et moue eos motu uehementi.	But if the fetus does not exit, then take hold of her feet and move them with a vigorous motion.  
Deinde preme quod est supra hypocundria paulatim, donec ascendat foetus ad superiora.	Then press upon what is above the hypocondrium gently until the fetus ascends to the upper parts. 
Deinde intromittat manus suas, et aequet foetum paulatim: et praecipe mulieri, ut comprimatur, donec egrediatur foetus.	Then let her insert her hands and equalize the fetus gently; and instruct the woman to compress until the fetus exits. 
¶ Exitus foetus latitudinaliter pendens ex manibus.	The exit of the fetus hanging laterally from the hands. 
Ingenietur in reductione manus eius.	Begin by reducing her hand.
Si autem non potest reducere eam, tunc eleua mulierem, et fac eam ambulare.	But if she cannot reduce it, then raise the woman and have her walk. 
Si uero ambulare non potest, tunc fac eam iacere super lectum: et concute crura eius concussione uehementi.	But if she cannot walk, then have her lie upon the bed and strike her legs with a vigorous concussion. 
Deinde administra linimentum quod praeparasti ex mucillaginibus.	Then administer the liniment which you prepared from gums.  
Quod si accipit eam partus, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem.	But if she receives labor pains, then have her sit upon a seat. 
Deinde stude in reductione manus, et aequa foetum secundum figuram naturalem: et fac sternutare mulierem, et praecipe ei, ut comprimat se, donec egrediatur.	Then strive in the reduction of the hand, and equalize the swelling according to the natural shape; and have the woman cough, and instruct her to compress herself until it comes out. 
¶ Exitus foetus super collum suum, expansis manibus, et est facies eius ad dorsum matris suae.	The exit of the fetus over its neck, with hands spread, and its face toward the back of its mother.  
Oportet ut teneat Obstetrix manum foetus, deinde reuoluat eum paulatim, et aequet eum cum facilitate.	It is necessary for the midwife to hold the hand of the fetus, then gradually turn it and align it with ease. 
Cum ergo aequatur, tunc pone super uuluam eius quod narrauimus ex oleo et mucillaginibus.	When, therefore, it is aligned, then place on its vulva what we have described made of oil and mucilages. 
Deinde praecipe ei, ut moueatur paulatim.	Then instruct her to move gradually.  
Cum ergo feceris illud, tunc fac eam sedere super sedem, et praecipe ei ut inclinetur ad latus dextrum.	When you have done this, then have her sit upon a seat and instruct her to lean towards her right side. 
Deinde praecipe ei, ut comprimatur: et fac eam sternutare cum condisi.	Then instruct her to compress herself; and have her cough when it is condensed.  
¶ Exitus foetus praeparati super latus.	The exit of the prepared fetus over its side. 
Quando descendit ad orificium matricis secundum hunc modum cum secundina, tunc scinde secundinam cum ungue tuo, donec euacuetur ex humiditate.	When it descends to the orifice of the matrix in this way with the secundina, then cut the secundina with your fingernail until it is evacuated from moisture. 
Si ergo suspenditur super faciem foetus, et collum eius, tunc incide eam ex umbilico: ut non retineatur, et moriatur.	If it therefore hangs over the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel so that it is not retained and dies. 
Deinde impelle foetum ad interiora, donec ponas eam secundum quod oportet: et praecipe mulieri, ut comprimat se aliquotiens: ipse enim egredietur exitu leui.	Then push the fetus toward the interior until you place it according to what is necessary; and instruct the woman to compress herself several times: for it itself will exit with an easy passage. 
¶ Exitus Geminorum, aut foetuum multorum.	The Exit of Twins, or Many Fetuses. 
Scias, quod Gemini multotiens nascuntur: et quandoque nascuntur tres, et quatuor.	Know that twins very often are born; and sometimes three, and four are born.  
Verumtamen illud extraneum est, et raro contingit.	However, that is extraordinary and rarely happens. 
Quinque uero est res extra naturam, et non uiuunt penitus: et continet eos, quamuis multiplicentur, secundina una: et separantur per sifach, distinguens inter eos ligatum in umbilico cuiusque eorum.	Five is a thing against nature and they do not live entirely; and it contains them, however many they may be, with one secundina; and they are separated by the sifach, distinguishing between them the ligature in the navel of each of them.  
Et quandoque egrediuntur sicut egreditur foetus unus exitu naturali, facili: et egrediuntur exitu illaudabili, sicut narrauimus.	And sometimes they exit as easily as a fetus exits naturally; and sometimes they exit with an unfortunate outcome, as we have described. 
Quod si difficiles fuerint quidam eorum apud partum, et perueniunt ad illud quod diximus ex figuris innaturalibus, tunc cura eos sicut narrauimus: et sit ob stetrix subtilis, et faciat quod facit cum facilitate et tarditate, et ingenietur secundum omnem figuram cum eo quod praeparatur ei ex ingenio ducente ad salutem.	But if some of them are difficult at childbirth and reach that which we said of unnatural figures, then care for them as we have described: and let there be a skilled midwife, and let her do what she does with ease and delay, and devise according to every shape with that which is prepared for her by ingenuity leading to health. 
¶ Rememoratio eius quod formatur in matrice ex embrionibus, et abortiuntur.	Remembrance of that which is formed in the womb from embryos, and miscarry. 
Quandoque formatur in matrice unus, et duo, et tres, et quatuor, et quinque, et sex, et septem, et plures decem: et iam uerificatum est apud me, quod mulier abortiendo emisit septem, et alia quindecim, omnes formatos.	Sometimes one is formed in the womb, and two, and three, and four, and five, and six, and seven, and more than ten: and it has already been verified by me that a woman miscarrying emitted seven, and another fifteen, all formed. 
Quod factum est mensuratione gloriosi sapientis.	Which was done by the measurement of the glorious wise one.  
Hoc ergo totum oportet ut sit in scientia Obstetricis.	Therefore all this must be in the knowledge of Obstetrics. 
Fortasse enim perueniet ad eam simile illius: opponat ergo ei cum illo quod oportet	For perhaps she may come across one like that; therefore oppose to her what is necessary.  
¶ De extractione foetus mortui.	On the extraction of a dead fetus. 
Caput LXXVI.	Chapter Seventy-Six. 
Quando curas foetum mortuum cum eo quod dixi in diuisione ex medicatione, et non egreditur, et cogeris uti operatione cum manu, tunc oportet ut consideres.	When you care for a dead fetus with what I said in the division from medication, and it does not exit, and you are forced to use surgery with your hand, then it is necessary that you consider.  
Si ergo mulier est sanae uirtutis, et non est cum aliquo ex accidentibus, ex quibus timetur super eam perditio: tunc oportet ut resupinetur mulier super lectum, super dorsum suum, et sit caput eius inclinatum inferius, et crura eius eleuata: et ministra teneat eam a duabus partibus, aut ligetur ad lectum, ut non extrahatur corpus eius apud extractionem foetus.	If therefore the woman is of sound health and is not with any accidents from which her loss is feared: then it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back on a bed, and let her head be inclined downwards, and let her legs be raised; and let assistants hold her from two sides, or let her be tied to the bed so that her body is not pulled out at the extraction of the fetus.  
Deinde humecta os matricis ex oleis humidis cum mucillagine alteae, et foenugraeci, et seminis lini.	Then moisten the mouth of the womb with oily substances with a decoction of marshmallow, fenugreek, and flaxseed.  
Deinde inungat Obstetrix manum suam cum istis oleis et mucillaginibus: deinde intromittat eam in matricem cum facilitate.	Then the midwife shall anoint her hand with these oils and mucilages; then she shall introduce it into the womb easily. 
Deinde quaerat cum ea locum in quo figat uncinos ex foetu, et loca conuenientia ad illud.	Then she shall seek with it a place in which to fasten the hooks from the fetus, and places suitable for that. 
Considera ergo tunc, si foetus est praeparatus ut descendat super caput suum: tunc fige uncinos in oculos eius, aut in collo eius, aut in ore eius, aut in palato ipsius, aut sub barba eius, aut in furcula ipsius, aut in locis propinquis costis, et sub hypocundriis.	Therefore consider then if the fetus is prepared to descend upon its head; then fix the hooks into its eyes, or into its neck, or into its mouth, or into its palate, or under its beard, or into its clavicle, or into places near the ribs, and under the hypochondria. 
Si autem descensus est super pedes eius, tunc in pectine, et costis eius mediis.	But if the descent is upon its feet, then into its breastbone, and its middle ribs. 
Et oportet, ut teneat uncinum cum manu dextra: et ponat curuitatem eius in eo quod est inter digitos sinistrae manus: et intromittat cum manu cum facilitate, et figat uncinum in aliquo illorum locorum quae diximus, donec perueniat ad rem uacuam.	And it is necessary that she hold the hook with her right hand; and place the curve of it into that which is between the fingers of her left hand; and introduce it with her hand easily, and fasten the hook into one of those places which we have said until she reaches a void space. 
Deinde figat in oppositione eius uncinum alium, aut tertium, si indiges: ut sit contractio aequalis, et non declinet ad partem.	Then she shall fasten opposite it another hook, or a third if necessary; so that there be equal contraction and it does not incline to one side.  
Deinde extendatur extensione aequali, et non sit extensio secundum rectitudinem tantum, imo moueatur ad omnem partem, ut alleuietur exitus eius: sicut fit cum dente apud eradicationem eius.	Then let it be extended with equal extension, and let there not be extension according to straightness only, but rather let it be moved to every side so that its exit is eased; just as is done when extracting a tooth.  
Et oportet in eo quod est inter illud, ut mollificetur extensio.	And it is necessary that in that which is between it, the extension be softened. 
Quod si retineatur ex eo pars, tunc oportet ut inungat Obstetrix quosdam digitos cum oleo, et intromittat eos ex parte, ut reuoluat cum eis quod retinetur.	But if a part is retained from it, then the midwife must anoint certain fingers with oil and introduce them from the side so that she may turn what is retained with them. 
Si ergo egreditur pars foetus, tunc permutentur uncini ad locum alium qui sit altior: fac hoc donec egrediatur foetus totus.	Therefore if a part of the fetus exits, then let the hooks be changed to another place which is higher; do this until the whole fetus exits. 
Si ergo egreditur manus ante alia, et non est possibile reducere eam, propter coartationem eius: tunc oportet, ut inuoluatur super eam pannus.	Therefore if the hand exits before the other parts and it is not possible to reduce it because of its constriction; then a cloth must be wrapped over it. 
Deinde extrahe eam donec quando egreditur tota, incide eam aut in iunctura plantae, aut in cubito: et ita oportet ut facias in manu altera, et in duobus pedibus.	Then extract it until the whole thing comes out, cut it either at the junction of the sole or on the elbow: and thus you must do in one hand, and in both feet. 
Si autem caput foetus est magnum, aut accidit ei coartatio in exitu, aut est in capite eius aqua aggregata: tunc oportet ut intromittat inter digitos Spatumile spinosum, et findat cum eo caput, et extrahat aquam: aut disrumpat ipsum cum instrumento quod nominatur Almisdac: cuius forma uenit cum formis reliquorum instrumentorum in capitulo quod est post hoc.	But if the head of the fetus is large, or constriction occurs at the outlet, or there is water collected in its head: then it is necessary that you insert the Spatumile spinosum between your fingers, and pierce the head with it, and extract the water: or break it up with an instrument called Almisdac: the form of which comes with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter which follows this. 
Similiter faciat si foetus est magni capitis natura, tunc oportet ut seces algengematu: aut extrahas ipsum cum misdach, sicut diximus.	Similarly, if the fetus is of a large-headed nature, it is necessary that you make an incision with an algengemat: or extract it with a misdach, as we have said. 
Deinde attrahas ossa cum forcipibus.	Then draw out the bones with forceps. 
Quod si egrediatur caput, et coartetur apud furculam: tunc findatur, donec effundatur humiditas quae est in pectore.	But if the head comes out, and is constricted at the fork: then pierce it until the moisture which is in the chest flows out. 
Si autem non complicatur, neque obedit ad exitum: tunc incide caput frustatim, secundum quod possibile est tibi.	But if it does not become entangled, nor yield to the outlet: then cut the head into pieces as best you can.  
Quod si inferius uentris est apostematum, aut est in eo hydropisis: tunc oportet ut perfores ipsum, donec currat humiditas ex eo.	But if there is an abscess below the belly, or there is dropsy in it: then you must pierce it until the moisture runs out of it. 
Si uero foetus est super pedes suos, tunc attractio eius est facilis, et directio eius ad os matricis est leuis.	But if the fetus is on its feet, then its attraction is easy, and its direction to the mouth of the uterus is slight.  
Si autem coartatur apud uentrem, aut pectus: tunc oportet ut extrahas ipsum cum panno quem inuoluisti super manum tuam: et findat uentrem, aut pectus, donec currat quod est in eis.	But if it is constricted at the belly or chest: then you must extract it with a cloth which you have put over your hand: and pierce the belly or chest until what is in them runs out.  
Si autem auferuntur reliqua membra, et redit caput: tunc intromittat Obstetrix manum sinistram.	But if the remaining limbs are removed and the head returns: then let the midwife insert her left hand. 
Si ergo os matricis est apertum, tunc intromittat manum in profundum matricis, et quaerat cum ea caput, et attrahat ipsum cum digitis usque ad os matricis: deinde intromittat in eo uncinum unum, aut uncinos duos, et attrahat ipsum cum eo.	Therefore, if the mouth of the uterus is open, let her insert her hand deep into the uterus, and seek out the head with it, and draw it up to the mouth of the uterus with her fingers: then let her insert one hook or two hooks into it and draw it out with them. 
Quod si os matricis coartatur, propter apostema calidum quod accidit ei: tunc non oportet ut laboretur super ipsum, imo oportet tunc administrare effusionem rerum humidarum, pinguium: et administra emplastra: et sedeat in aquis quae mollificant et humectant.	If the mouth of the uterus is constricted due to a hot abscess that occurs there, then it is not necessary for him to work on it, but rather he should then administer a pouring-on of humid and fatty things, and apply poultices, and sit in waters which soften and moisten. 
Quod si foetus est super latus suum, tunc possibile est ut aequetur: tunc administretur quod diximus in foetu uiuo.	If the fetus is on its side, then it is possible that it may be straightened; then let what we said about the living fetus be administered. 
Quod si non est possibile illud, tunc incidatur frustatim, et extrahatur.	But if that is not possible, then let it be cut in pieces, and taken out.  
Et oportet ut non dimittas aliquid ex secundina intus omnino.	And it is necessary that you do not leave anything from the secundines inside at all. 
Cum ergo compleueris operationem tuam, tunc administra quod diximus in apostematibus calidis quae accidunt in matricibus.	Therefore when you have completed your operation, then administer what we said about hot abscesses which occur in uteruses. 
Quod si accidat fluxus sanguinis, tunc descendat in aquis stipticis, et administra reliquam curationem.	If a flow of blood should happen, then let her descend into astringent waters and administer the remaining care.  
Et ego quidem iam uidi mulierem, in cuius uentre mortuus erat foetus: deinde impregnata est super ipsum uice alia, postea mortuus est foetus alius etiam.	And I myself have indeed already seen a woman in whose belly a fetus had died, then she became pregnant again on top of it with another, afterwards the other fetus also died. 
Accidit ergo ei post tempus longum apostema in umbilico suo, et inflatum est, donec apertum est: et coepit emittere pus.	Therefore it happened to her after a long time that an abscess occurred in her navel and it became swollen until it opened and began to emit pus. 
Vocatus sum ergo ad curationem eius, et medicatus sum ei tempore longo: et non consolidatum est uulnus.	I was therefore called for her care and I treated her for a long time, and the wound did not consolidate.
Posui ergo super ipsum ex quibusdam emplastris fortis attractionis: et exiuit ex loco os.	Therefore I put on it some poultices of strong attraction and an opening came out in its place. 
Deinde praeterierunt ei dies aliquot, et exiuit os aliud.	Then several days passed and another opening came out.  
Miratus sum ergo inde, cum in uentre non sit os.	I therefore wondered because there was no opening in the belly. 
Cogitaui ergo, quia erant ex ossibus foetus mortui.	I therefore thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.  
Inquisiui ergo uulnus, et extraxi ossa multa, muliere existente in melioribus dispositionibus suis: et iam uixit taliter tempore longo, et mittit ex loco pus parum.	I therefore examined the wound and extracted many bones with the woman being in a better state; and she now lives thus for a long time, and emits little pus from its place. 
Et ego non firmaui hic hoc extraneum, nisi quoniam in eo est scientia, et adiutorium ad illud, quod administrat medicus artifex cum manu ex curatione.	I did not include this here except because it contains knowledge and assistance for what the craftsman physician administers with his hand from healing. 
¶ De formis Instrumentorum necessariorum in extractione foetus.	On the forms of instruments necessary in the extraction of a fetus. 
Caput LXXVII.	Chapter Seventy-Seven. 
Hic inferius est forma Strictorii, quo aequantur libri, cui aequaliter sunt duae uertigines in duabus extremitatibus duorum lignorum.	Below is the form of a Strictor, by which books are equaled, to which are equally two vortices at the two ends of two pieces of wood.  
Verumtamen haec Vertigo oportet ut sit subtilior strictorio: et ut fiat, aut ex ebano, aut ex ligno bussi.	However, these Vortices ought to be more subtle than the Strictor: and so it is made, either from ebony or boxwood.
